الكبيرة التي الفائدة. بذلت في إتمام هذا الكتاب وتصحيحه وإخراجه لما فيه من عظيم النفع وعميم الفائدة.وفي الختام نسأل الله لا أن يكون هذا العمل خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، وأن ينفع به العباد، ويعم خيره في البلاد، ويجعله لنا ذخراً يوم المعاد ، وصَلَّى الله على سيدنا محمد، وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم. وكتبه الدكتور صلاح أبو الحاج الأردن، عمان
Utmost Care in the Introduction to 'Umda al-Ri'aya. By the grace of God, I was able to refer to the source of the speech, correct the words and phrases, and document them; for there occurred in it countless errors from the copyists. But by referring to the original sources, I was able to rectify that. And God knows best. 5. Extraction of hadiths from their sources, and recording the exact wording of the hadith as recorded in the authentic books of hadith and the Sunan if it was recorded with its meaning in the book. 6. Adding evidence for many issues of the book to the extent of need, ability, and time sufficient to fulfill the need of its reader. Clarification and explanation of some of the hidden words and phrases according to what the context requires. Correction of the commentator in some of his choices and ijtihads that contradict the relied-upon position in fatwa, by mentioning the evidence for that. 9. Correcting the Qur'anic verses according to the Uthmani orthography; for most of the errors in the book were in writing the Qur'anic verses. By adopting the Uthmani orthography, we were able to overcome this problem. 10. Dividing the book into short paragraphs, which helps the reader understand the speech without boredom, and inserting appropriate punctuation marks, and observing modern orthographic rules, to facilitate the seekers in obtaining their objectives. And I draw attention here that I did not record what the copyists wrote between the lines in terms of resolving pronouns, explaining the meaning of some words, and the like. Rather, I restricted myself to what began with sequential numbering, and began with the word 'qawluhu' (his saying); because it appears that this is the gloss of al-Laknawi, while the other is from the additions of the copyists. This was suggested to us by our virtuous, great verifying Sheikh, Sheikh Shu'ayb al-Arna'ut, may God protect him and take care of him, as he said that there is no need for what is mentioned between the lines, because it prolongs the book without benefit; for they are comments devoid of true scientific benefit, and recording them would only increase the size of the book. And God knows best. It is also indicated here that Imam 'Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi passed away before completing the book, and he reached the Book of Sale. So his commentary is only on the first half of the book. For the second half, the senior scholars of India competed to comment on it to complete the book and benefit from it. Then the third quarter was commented upon by 'Abd al-Hamid ibn 'Abd al-Halim al-Laknawi and he named it 'Zubdat al-Nihaya li-'Umda al-Ri'aya', and he is the author of 'al-Hall al-Daruri li-Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. You will come across his biography at the beginning of his gloss. And the last quarter was commented upon by the scholar, the jurist 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Abd al-Rahim al-Laknawi, and he named it 'Husn al-Diraya li-Awakhir Sharh al-Wiqaya'. So look, may God have mercy on you, at the great efforts that were exerted in completing this book, correcting it, and producing it, due to the immense benefit and widespread advantage it contains. In conclusion, we ask God that this work be purely for His noble face, and that He benefit the people with it, and that its goodness spread in the lands, and make it a treasure for us on the Day of Return. And may God bless our master Muhammad, and his family and companions, and grant them peace. Written by Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, Jordan, Amman.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the verified edition of 'Umda al-Ri'aya. The editor, Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, outlines his methodology in preparing this critical edition. He mentions that he corrected errors by referring to original sources, extracted hadiths from their primary sources, added evidentiary support for rulings, clarified obscure terms, corrected the commentator's deviations from the relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions, and corrected Qur'anic verses according to the Uthmani script. He also divided the text into short paragraphs for readability. Notably, he excluded interlinear annotations made by copyists because they were of little scientific value, a decision endorsed by the eminent scholar Shu'ayb al-Arna'ut. The introduction also explains the division of scholarly labor: the original author, Imam 'Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, only completed the first half of the book (up to the Book of Sale). The second half was completed by two other scholars: 'Abd al-Hamid al-Laknawi wrote a gloss on the third quarter, and 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Laknawi on the last quarter. Thus, the book is a composite work of multiple Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
حاشية (hashiyah): A supercommentary or gloss on a primary text; in this context, 'Umda al-Ri'aya is a hashiya on Sharh al-Wiqaya.
تخريج الحديث (takhrij al-hadith): Tracing a hadith to its original source in the hadith collections, verifying its wording and chain of transmission.
الرسم العثماني (al-rasm al-uthmani): The standard orthography of the Qur'an as established by the Caliph Uthman ibn Affan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A critical edition of a Hanafi text is the result of meticulous scholarly effort; using it ensures that legal rulings are built on sound foundations.

Identifying the Supercommentators of 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah'
Identifying scholars who completed the hashiah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi scholars who wrote supercommentaries on the third and fourth quarters of 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah' and name their respective works.

Core Idea
Two Laknawi scholars completed the supercommentary on 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah' for the missing quarters.

Scholarly works often have a chain of commentators and supercommentators. In this editor's introduction, we learn about two Hanafi jurists from the Indian subcontinent who completed the hashiah (supercommentary) on the last two quarters of 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah'. This biographical note helps us understand the collaborative nature of Islamic scholarship and the continuity of the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its parts
The book in question is 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah', a supercommentary on a commentary of Al-Wiqayah. The editor mentions that supercommentaries were written on each quarter; note the third and fourth quarters specifically.
The first two quarters are not mentioned here; only the third and fourth are attributed to specific scholars.
2
Extract the name of the first scholar
From the text: 'Abd al-Hamid ibn 'Abd al-Halim al-Laknawi wrote the hashiah on the third quarter. He also authored 'al-Hall al-Daruri li-Mukhtasar al-Quduri'.
His work on the third quarter is titled 'Zubdat al-Nihayah li-'Umdat al-Ri'ayah'.
3
Extract the name of the second scholar
The second scholar is 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Abd al-Rahim al-Laknawi, who wrote on the last (fourth) quarter. His hashiah is named 'Husn al-Dirayah li-Awakhir Sharh al-Wiqayah'.
His father is 'Abd al-Rahim, also a scholar.
4
Understand the significance
These supercommentaries represent the extensive efforts of later Hanafi scholars to preserve, explain, and transmit the legal reasoning of earlier masters. The editor praises their contribution.
The passage ends with a prayer and the editor's signature.

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction. The editor, Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, acknowledges the contributions of two major scholars who wrote supercommentaries (hashiyah) on different quarters of the book 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah'. The first is 'Abd al-Hamid al-Laknawi, who wrote on the third quarter and titled his work 'Zubdat al-Nihayah li-'Umdat al-Ri'ayah'. He is also known for his commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The second is 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Laknawi, who wrote on the last (fourth) quarter and titled his work 'Husn al-Dirayah li-Awakhir Sharh al-Wiqayah'. The editor praises their efforts and expresses hope that the work is accepted by Allah and beneficial to people. This biographical note is essential for understanding the tradition of supercommentaries on Hanafi legal texts and the scholarly chains of transmission.

Key Terms
حاشية (hashiyah): A supercommentary or marginal gloss on a primary commentary. Here, it refers to the detailed annotations written on specific quarters of the book 'Umdah al-Ri'ayah'.
ربع (rub'): Quarter; a division of the book into four parts, each possibly covered by a separate supercommentary.

Introducing 'Umda al-Ri'aya': A Hanafi Fiqh Commentary
Title page with bibliographic details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the title, author, and components of 'Umda al-Ri'aya' and explain its place in the Hanafi fiqh tradition.

Core Idea
Umda al-Ri'aya is a late Hanafi commentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya with a modern marginal gloss.

This lesson introduces the book 'Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya', a significant text in the Hanafi school. Understanding the structure of this commentary will help you navigate its contents and appreciate its scholarly lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main title
The book is called 'Umda al-Ri'aya', meaning 'The Pillar of Care' – a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya.
The title appears at the top of the page.
2
Recognize the base text
It is a commentary on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya', a standard Hanafi fiqh manual by Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi.
Sharh al-Wiqaya itself is a commentary on al-Wiqaya.
3
Note the author and his time
The author is Imam Abd al-Hamid ibn Ta'bad al-Ta'alim al-Kanawi (d. 1304 AH), a late Hanafi scholar whose work reflects the later tarjih positions.

The margin contains 'Ghayat al-'Inaya' by Dr. Salah Muhammad Abu al-Hajj, a modern scholarly gloss on Umda al-Ri'aya.

The Opening Praise: Scholars as Heirs of the Prophets
Opening hamdalah and praise of scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the opening hamdalah in a Hanafi fiqh commentary and identify the key concepts that establish the authority of scholars.

Core Idea
Scholars are heirs of the prophets, inheriting knowledge and the duty to guide.

This passage opens the commentary with praise to Allah and the Prophet, emphasizing the elevated status of scholars. It sets the stage for the entire work by rooting the author’s authority in the prophetic heritage. Understanding this prologue is essential to appreciating the tradition in which Hanafi fiqh is studied and transmitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parts of the opening
The passage begins with hamdalah (praise of Allah), followed by salawat (blessings on the Prophet), and then praise of scholars. Each part serves a distinct purpose: thanking Allah, honoring the Prophet, and setting the theme of scholarly authority.
This tripartite structure is standard in Islamic scholarly works.
2
Extract the key claim about scholars
The central claim is that Allah has expanded the breasts of scholars to accept the secrets of Shari'ah and made them 'heirs of the prophets.' This is directly from the hadith: 'The scholars are the heirs of the prophets.'
The phrase 'ورثة الأنبياء' is a well-known hadith, cited to establish the dignity of scholars.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof cited
The author quotes verse 28 of Surah Fatir: 'Indeed, only those fear Allah among His servants who have knowledge.' This verse is used to prove that true fear of Allah (khashyah) is rooted in knowledge, elevating the rank of scholars.
The verse is cited as evidence for the virtue of knowledge, not for a specific fiqh ruling.
4
Evaluate the hadith about the Companions as stars
The footnote discusses the hadith 'My companions are like stars; whichever of them you follow, you will be guided.' Although the chain is weak according to muhaddithun, it is accepted by people of kashf. The author uses it to support the authority of the Companions and, by extension, the scholars who follow their path.
This shows the Hanafi approach to reconciling hadith criticism with the consensus of the Ahl al-Sunnah.
5
Connect to the purpose of the commentary
The entire opening establishes that this commentary is a continuation of prophetic knowledge. The author positions himself as a scholar who, by explaining the rulings, fulfills the duty of the heirs of the prophets.
This frames the subsequent fiqh discussions as part of a sacred inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمد لله الذي شرح صدور العلماء لقبول أسرار شريعته الغراء، وجعلهم حملة شريعته ومهرة طريقته الزهراء، ولقبهم بما زادَ به فضلهم وفخرهم على لسان حبيبه وصفيه، فأخبر أنهم ورثة الأنبياء، ووعد لمن تفقه في الدين المتين، وغاص في بحار الشرع المبين بجزيل النعماء ، وأعد لهم منازل شريفة، ومراتب لطيفة يوم الحساب والجزاء.
أحمده حمداً كثيراً وأشكره شكراً كبيراً على ما خص أهل العلم بفضائل لا تعدُّ ولا تحصى في الدنيا والعُقبى وروح نفوسهم بقوله في كتابه : إِنَّمَا يَخْشَى اللَّهَ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ الْعُلَمَاءُ (1) أشهد أنه لا إله إلا هو وحده لا شريك له في الابتداء والانتهاء، وأشهد أن سيدنا محمداً عبده ورسوله ، تاج الشريعة، وبرهان الطريقة البيضاء، المخصوص بـشرف السعاية، وحسن الرعاية، شمس الأئمة وسراج الخليقة بلا امتراء، الذي أوضح لنا الحلال والحرام، ونبه على مشتبهات الأحكام، وقنن قوانين الاهتداء.
اللهم صل وسلم وبارك عليه صلاة دائمة متوالية بلا انقطاع ولا إحصاء، وعلى آله وصحبه الذين هاجروا لنصرته، ونصروا في هجرته ، نجوم الاهتداء(2)
(1) فاطر: من الآية 28.
(2) إشارة إلى حديث: «أصحابي كالنجوم بأيهم اقتديتم اهتديتم» أخرجه الدارقطني في كتاب «غرائب مالك»، والبزار والقضاعي في «مسند الشهاب» (2: 275)، وأبو ذر الهروي في «كتاب السنة»، والبيهقي في «المدخل» (1: 115) وقال : هذا حديث متنه مشهور، وأسانيده ضعيفة، لم يثبت في هذا إسنادا، وعبد بن حميد في «مسنده» (1: 250)، وغيرهم، وأسانيده وإن كانت ضعيفة كما بسطه الحافظ ابن حجر في «تلخيص الحبير» (4: 190) و«الكاف الشاف بتخريج أحاديث الكشاف» (2: 603) لكنه صحيح عند أهل الكشف، كما ذكره عبد الوهاب الشعراني في «الميزان» (1: 30)، فقال : وهذا الحديث وإن كان فيه مقال عند المحدثين، فهو صحيح عند أهل الكشف، وليس هو بموضوع.
Praise be to Allah who expanded the breasts of scholars to accept the secrets of His brilliant Shari'ah, and made them bearers of His Shari'ah and skilled in His radiant path, and honored them with what increased their virtue and pride through the tongue of His beloved and chosen one, so He informed that they are the heirs of the prophets, and promised for those who gain deep understanding in the firm religion and dive into the seas of the clear law abundant blessings, and prepared for them noble stations and subtle ranks on the Day of Reckoning and Requital. I praise Him abundantly and thank Him greatly for bestowing upon the people of knowledge virtues that cannot be counted or enumerated in this world and the Hereafter, and He revived their souls with His saying in His Book: 'Indeed, only those fear Allah among His servants who have knowledge' (Surah Fatir, verse 28). I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner in the beginning and the end, and I bear witness that our master Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, the crown of Shari'ah, the proof of the white path, distinguished with the honor of intercession and good care, the sun of the imams and the lamp of creation without doubt, who made clear to us the permissible and forbidden, and alerted us to ambiguous rulings, and codified the laws of guidance. O Allah, send blessings, peace, and barakah upon him with continuous, successive prayers without cessation or counting, and upon his family and companions who emigrated for his victory and supported him in his emigration, the stars of guidance. (Footnote 1: Surah Fatir, part of verse 28. Footnote 2: Reference to the hadith: 'My companions are like stars; whichever of them you follow, you will be guided.' Reported by al-Daraqutni in 'Ghara'ib Malik', al-Bazzar and al-Quda'i in 'Musnad al-Shihab' (2:275), Abu Dharr al-Harawi in 'Kitab al-Sunnah', al-Bayhaqi in 'al-Madkhal' (1:115) who said: This hadith's text is well-known but its chains are weak, no sound chain has been established for it, and 'Abd ibn Humayd in his 'Musnad' (1:250), and others. Its chains, although weak as detailed by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in 'Talkhis al-Habir' (4:190) and 'al-Kafi al-Shaf bi-Takhrij Ahadith al-Kashshaf' (2:603), are nonetheless sound according to the people of kashf, as mentioned by 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani in 'al-Mizan' (1:30), who said: This hadith, although criticized by hadith scholars, is sound according to the people of kashf, and it is not fabricated.)
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the book (front matter), where the author begins with the traditional praise of Allah (hamdalah) and blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad (salawat). He thanks Allah for granting scholars the capacity to understand the deeper aspects of Shari'ah and for making them the heirs of the prophets, a reference to the well-known hadith: 'The scholars are the heirs of the prophets.' The author then cites the Quranic verse from Surah Fatir (28) to emphasize the virtue of knowledge. He also praises the Prophet for clarifying the halal and haram and for establishing the principles of guidance. The footnote discusses the authenticity of the hadith 'My companions are like stars,' noting that although its chains are weak according to hadith scholars, it is considered sound by the people of kashf (spiritual unveiling). This introduction sets the tone for the commentary that follows, establishing the authority of scholars in interpreting the sacred law.

Key Terms
ورثة الأنبياء (warathat al-anbiya'): The author uses this phrase to state that scholars are the heirs of the prophets, inheriting their knowledge and mission.
شريعة (shari'ah): The divine law of Islam as revealed to the Prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what did Allah inform regarding scholars based on the hadith cited in the opening?
A) They are the stars of guidance.
B) They are the heirs of the prophets.
C) They are the kings of the earth.
D) They are the companions of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The opening hamdalah establishes that scholars are the true heirs of the prophets, entrusted with the knowledge and interpretation of Shari'ah.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
The Author's Introduction: Praise, Purpose, and the Heirs of the Prophets
Opening hamd, salawat, and author's introduction to the commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a classical Hanafi fiqh commentary's introduction and explain why scholars are considered heirs of the prophets.

Core Idea
Scholars are the true inheritors of the prophets — the introduction frames the entire work as a service to sacred knowledge.

The opening of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' is not just praise; it establishes the authority and purpose of the work. The author, Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, situates his commentary within the tradition of prophetic inheritance, honoring the scholars, especially Imam Abu Hanifa, and setting the stage for the legal analysis to follow. The footnote on the hadith of the stars demonstrates scholarly rigor in verifying transmitted reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main sections
The introduction consists of praise of Allah (hamd), blessings on the Prophet (salawat), and a transitional phrase 'Amma ba'd' leading into the main subject.
This tripartite structure is standard in classical Islamic works.
2
Analyze the praise of scholars
The author highlights that Allah 'expanded the breasts of scholars' and that they are the 'heirs of the prophets.' Reflect on how this elevates the status of fiqh scholarship.
This theme of inheritance is rooted in a well-known hadith.
3
Recognize the Prophet's role in clarifying rulings
The text notes that the Prophet made clear 'the lawful and the unlawful' and alerted to 'ambiguous rulings.' This underscores the source of all fiqh.
The Prophet's explanations are foundational for Hanafi usul.
4
Locate the praise of Imam Abu Hanifa and the mujtahids
The author specifically praises Imam Abu Hanifa as 'the master of the followers' and 'head of the mujtahids,' granting him central importance.
This shows the Hanafi school's veneration of its founder.
5
Understand the footnote on the hadith of the stars
The long footnote discusses the authenticity of the hadith 'My companions are like stars,' concluding it is not fabricated despite weak chains. This exemplifies scholarly verification.
This is a parenthetical note and not part of the main content.

الحمد لله الذي شرح صدور العلماء لقبول أسرار شريعته الغراء، وجعلهم حملة شريعته ومهرة طريقته الزهراء، ولقبهم بما زادَ به فضلهم وفخرهم على لسان حبيبه وصفيه، فأخبر أنهم ورثة الأنبياء، ووعد لمن تفقه في الدين المتين، وغاص في بحار الشرع المبين بجزيل النعماء ، وأعد لهم منازل شريفة، ومراتب لطيفة يوم الحساب والجزاء.
أحمده حمداً كثيراً وأشكره شكراً كبيراً على ما خص أهل العلم بفضائل لا تعدُّ ولا تحصى في الدنيا والعُقبى وروح نفوسهم بقوله في كتابه : إِنَّمَا يَخْشَى اللَّهَ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ (1) العلموا أشهد أنه لا إله إلا هو وحده لا شريك له في الابتداء والانتهاء، وأشهد أن سيدنا محمداً عبده ورسوله ، تاج الشريعة، وبرهان الطريقة البيضاء، المخصوص بـشرف السعاية، وحسن الرعاية، شمس الأئمة وسراج الخليقة بلا امتراء، الذي أوضح لنا الحلال والحرام، ونبه على مشتبهات الأحكام، وقنن قوانين الاهتداء.
اللهم صل وسلم وبارك عليه صلاة دائمة متوالية بلا انقطاع ولا إحصاء، وعلى آله وصحبه الذين هاجروا لنصرته، ونصروا في هجرته ، نجوم الاهتداء(۲) وقروم (۱) الاقتداء ، أوضحوا سُبُل الهداية، وبلغوا في نصرة الدين أقصى النهاية ، وجاهدوا في إعلاء كلمةِ الله من غير سُمعة ولا رياء.
وعلى من تبعهم من الأئمة المجتهدين الذين دوّنوا الدواوين، وقتنوا القوانين، واستنبطوا أحكام الوقائع والحوادث من العبارة والإشارة، والدلالة والاقتضاء، جزاهم الله عني وعن سائر المسلمين خير الجزاء، لا سيما على إمامنا الأعظم، وإمامنا الأقدم، سيد التابعين، ورأس المجتهدين ، أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، رئيس أرباب الاتقاء، وعلى مقلديهم ومتبعيهم ، ومن سلك مسلكهم، وتمذهب بمذهبهم من المفسرين والمحدثين والمتكلمين والفقهاء.
أما بعد :
فيقول الراجي عفو ربِّه القوي، أبو الحسنات محمد عبد الحي اللكهنوي (٢) تجاوز على ما ظُنّ، وقد فصلت الكلام فيه في رسالتي «تحفة الأخيار في إحياء سنة سيد الأبرار» (٥٣ - ٦٥) ، وتعليقاتها المسماة بـ «نخبة الأنظار » (ص ٥٣ - ٦٥ ، فلتطالع منه رحمه الله تعالى. وقال ابن قطلوبغا الله في خلاصة الأفكار ( ص ٥٨) : رواه الدارقطني وابن عبد البر من حديث ابن عمر الله ، وقد روي معناه من حديث عمر ، ومن حديث ابن عباس ه ، ومن حديث أنس له ، وفي أسانيدهما مقال، لكن يشد بعضها بعضا». وحسنه الصغاني والطيبي، قال اللكنوي في تحفة الأخيار» (ص ٥٣ ) : روي ذلك بألفاظ مختلفة، وقد طال كلامهم على هذا الحديث تضعيفاً وجرحاً، حتى ظن بعضهم أنه حديث موضوع، وليس كذلك، نعم طرق روايته ضعيفة، ولا يلزم منه وضعها». وقال الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة في تعليقاته على تحفة الأخيار» (ص) ٥٤) : ورد هذا الحديث في الجملة وأنه ليس بموضوع». وقال ابن حجر في تلخيص الحبير» (٤) : ١٩١) : «ذكر عن البيهقي أنه قال : إن حديث مسلم يؤدّي بعض معناه ، يعني قوله : «النجوم أمنة للسماء ، فإذا ذهبن النجوم أتى السماء ما توعد، وأنا أمنة لأصحابي ، فإذا ذهبت أتى أصحابي ما يوعدون، وأصحابي أمنة لأمتي، فإذا ذهب أصحابي أتى أمتي ما يوعدون.» في صحيح مسلم ٤ : ١٩٦١ ، وصحيح ابن حبان ١٦ : ٢٣٤ ، و(مسند أحمد ٤ : ۳۹۸ ، وغيرها. وينظر : تعليق السيد عبد الله الغماري على تأييد الحقيقة العلية للسيوطي » ( ص ٩٦) ، و (خلاصة البدر المنير لابن الملقن (۲ : ٤۳۱ ) ، وكشف الخفاء» (۱) : (١٤٧) ، و (لسان الميزان (۲) : (۱۳۷)، و«الفوائد» لابن منْدَه ( ص (۲۹)، و«الشريعة للآجري (١١٤٨) ، والإبانة الكبرى» لابن بطة (۷۰۹).
Praise be to Allah who expanded the breasts of scholars to accept the secrets of His brilliant Shariah, and made them the bearers of His Shariah and the skilled ones of His bright path, and honored them with what increased their virtue and pride through the tongue of His beloved and chosen one, so He informed that they are the heirs of the prophets, and promised whoever gains deep understanding in the strong religion and dives into the seas of the clear Shariah with abundant blessings, and prepared for them noble ranks and subtle stations on the Day of Reckoning and Recompense. I praise Him abundantly and thank Him greatly for what He has specifically given the people of knowledge of virtues that cannot be counted or enumerated in this world and the Hereafter, and He comforted their souls with His saying in His Book: 'Indeed, only those among His servants who have knowledge fear Allah' (1). I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner in the beginning and the end, and I bear witness that our master Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, the crown of the Shariah, the proof of the bright path, distinguished by the honor of striving and good care, the sun of the imams and the lamp of creation without doubt, who made clear to us the lawful and the unlawful, and alerted us to ambiguous rulings, and codified the laws of guidance. O Allah, send blessings and peace and benedictions upon him, a perpetual and continuous prayer without interruption or count, and upon his family and companions who emigrated for his victory and supported him in his migration, the stars of guidance (2) and the leaders of emulation, who clarified the paths of guidance, reached the utmost limit in supporting the religion, and strove to elevate the word of Allah without show or hypocrisy. And upon those who followed them from the mujtahid imams who compiled the compilations, codified the laws, and deduced the rulings of events and incidents from explicit text, indication, implication, and requirement. May Allah reward them from me and from all Muslims with the best reward, especially our greatest imam, our foremost imam, the master of the followers (tabi'in), the head of the mujtahids, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, the chief of the people of piety, and upon their emulators and followers, and those who tread their path and adopt their school from the exegetes, hadith scholars, theologians, and jurists. To proceed: The one hoping for the pardon of his Strong Lord, Abu al-Hasanat Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi (2) said... (then a long footnote about the hadith of the stars and the companions).
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the book 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah'. It begins with the traditional praise of Allah (hamdalah), blessings on the Prophet (salat wa salam), and praise of the scholars, especially the mujtahid imams. The author follows the classical style of Islamic scholarly works. He highlights that scholars are the heirs of the prophets, and that deep understanding in religion (tafaqquh) leads to noble ranks. He specifically praises Imam Abu Hanifa and his followers. Then he uses 'Amma ba'd' to transition to the main topic. The long footnote discusses the authenticity of the hadith 'My companions are like stars', citing various scholars and concluding that despite weak chains, it is not fabricated. The author then presumably begins the actual commentary. This entire section sets the theological and scholarly framework for the work.

Key Terms
الحلال والحرام (al-halal wa al-haram): The lawful and the forbidden according to Islamic law; the Prophet made these clear.
مشتبهات الأحكام (mushtabihat al-ahkam): Ambiguous or doubtful rulings that are not clearly halal or haram.
أما بعد (amma ba'd): A transitional phrase meaning 'to proceed' or 'now then', used to move from the introduction to the main subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of the phrase 'Amma ba'd' in this introduction?
A) It signals the end of the book.
B) It introduces a new topic after the opening praise.
C) It is a form of praise for the Prophet.
D) It indicates a change in authorship.

Key Takeaway
The introduction of a Hanafi fiqh commentary is both a theological statement and a declaration of scholarly lineage, establishing the work as part of the prophetic heritage.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Virtue of Tafaqquh in Religion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the meaning of tafaqquh fi al-din and explain why it is considered the best virtue according to the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Tafaqquh (deep understanding of religion) is the greatest virtue, as indicated by the hadith.

The author begins his preface by emphasizing the supreme importance of deep religious understanding. This lesson explores the significance of tafaqquh and the hadith that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim about tafaqquh
Locate the sentence where the author states that the best virtue is tafaqquh fi al-din. Understand that this is the central thesis of the introduction.
The author uses the phrase 'أفضل الفضائل وأكمل الشمائل'.
2
Examine the hadith cited
Find the hadith 'Whomsoever Allah desires good for, He grants him deep understanding in religion.' Note that the author attributes it to the 'imams of religion'.
This hadith is widely transmitted and considered authentic by many.
3
Recognize the scholarly implication
Understand that tafaqquh is not just memorization but includes teaching, learning, researching, and discussing. The author praises those who engage in these activities.
The word 'باحث' indicates active scholarly discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقروم (۱) الاقتداء ، أوضحوا سُبُل الهداية، وبلغوا في نصرة الدين أقصى النهاية ، وجاهدوا في إعلاء كلمةِ الله من غير سُمعة ولا رياء.
وعلى من تبعهم من الأئمة المجتهدين الذين دوّنوا الدواوين، وقتنوا القوانين، واستنبطوا أحكام الوقائع والحوادث من العبارة والإشارة، والدلالة والاقتضاء، جزاهم الله عني وعن سائر المسلمين خير الجزاء، لا سيما على إمامنا الأعظم، وإمامنا الأقدم، سيد التابعين، ورأس المجتهدين ، أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، رئيس أرباب الاتقاء، وعلى مقلديهم ومتبعيهم ، ومن سلك مسلكهم، وتمذهب بمذهبهم من المفسرين والمحدثين والمتكلمين والفقهاء.
أما بعد :
فيقول الراجي عفو ربِّه القوي، أبو الحسنات محمد عبد الحي اللكهنوي (۲) تجاوز الله عن ذنبه الجلي والخفي، ابن صدر العلم، بدر الفضلاء، شمس الفقهاء، تاج الكملاء، البحر الزخار الغيث المدرار، صاحب التصانيف النافعة، ذي المناقب والمحامد الوافرة، مولانا الحاج الحافظ محمد عبد الحليم ) ، أدخله الله دار النعيم، وأوصله إلى مقام كريم : إنه لا يخفى على أرباب النهي أن أفضل الفضائل وأكمل الشمائل هو التفقه في الدين، وإليه أشار سيد المرسلين، بقوله الذي أخرجته أئمة الدين: «من يُرد الله به خيراً يفقهه في الدين (۲) وهو الوصف الذي يمتاز به المرء بين الأقران والأماثل، ويكون مشاراً إليه في الفضل والكمال بالأنامل ، فطوبى لمن عَلَّمَه وتعلمه، وباحث فيه ودرسه. وقد صُنفت في علم الفقه كتب شريفة، وزُيرٌ ،نظيفة، وسيطة ووجيزة، وبسيطة وقصيرة، ومن أجل الكتب المتوسطة المشتملة على الأصول والفروع المعتبرة، التي هبت عليها رياح القبول، واستحسنها علماء النقول ، كتاب «الوقاية في مسائل الهداية» لبرهان الشريعة، وشرحها لتلميذه صدر الشريعة، برَّدَ اللهُ مضجعهما، وقدَّسَ اللهُ مبعثهما ، وقد نالا حظاً وافراً من الاشتهار لا كاشتهار الشمس على نصف النهار. وقد صرف جمع من الفقهاء عنان عزيمتهما إليهما فكتبوا شروحاً وتعليقات عليهما، وتداولوهما فيما بينهم درساً وتدريساً وتعلماً وتعليماً، وقد تركوا كلهم ما هو الواجب عليهم من ذكر أدلة الأحكام، وربط الفروع بالأصول بالإحكام :
فمنهم : من اقتصر فأخل.
ومنهم : مَن طول فأمل، ترى :
بعضهم : يكتفون على حل المواضع السهلة، ويتركون كشف المقامات المغلقة.
على ما ظنّ، وقد فصلت الكلام فيه في رسالتي «تحفة الأخيار في إحياء سنة سيد الأبرار» (٥٣ - ٦٥) ، وتعليقاتها المسماة بـ «نخبة الأنظار » (ص ٥٣ - ٦٥ ، فلتطالع منه رحمه الله تعالى. وقال ابن قطلوبغا الله في خلاصة الأفكار ( ص ٥٨) : رواه الدارقطني وابن عبد البر من حديث ابن عمر الله ، وقد رُوي معناه من حديث عمر ، ومن حديث ابن عباس ه ، ومن حديث أنس له ، وفي أسانيدهما مقال، لكن يشد بعضها بعضا». وحسنه الصغاني والطيبي، قال اللكنوي في تحفة الأخيار» (ص ٥٣ ) : روي ذلك بألفاظ مختلفة، وقد طال كلامهم على هذا الحديث تضعيفاً وجرحاً، حتى ظن بعضهم أنه حديث موضوع، وليس كذلك، نعم طرق روايته ضعيفة، ولا يلزم منه وضعها». وقال الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة في تعليقاته على تحفة الأخيار» (ص) ٥٤) : ورد هذا الحديث في الجملة وأنه ليس بموضوع». وقال ابن حجر في تلخيص الحبير» (٤) : ١٩١) : «ذكر عن البيهقي أنه قال : إن حديث مسلم يؤدّي بعض معناه ، يعني قوله : «النجوم أمنة للسماء ، فإذا ذهبن النجوم أتى السماء ما توعد، وأنا أمنة لأصحابي ، فإذا ذهبت أتى أصحابي ما يوعدون، وأصحابي أمنة لأمتي، فإذا ذهب أصحابي أتى أمتي ما يوعدون.» في صحيح مسلم ٤ : ١٩٦١ ، وصحيح ابن حبان ١٦ : ٢٣٤ ، و(مسند أحمد ٤ : ۳۹۸ ، وغيرها. وينظر : تعليق السيد عبد الله الغماري على تأييد الحقيقة العلية للسيوطي » ( ص ٩٦) ، و (خلاصة البدر المنير لابن الملقن (۲ : ٤۳۱ ) ، وكشف الخفاء» (۱) : (١٤٧) ، و (لسان الميزان (۲) : (۱۳۷)، و«الفوائد» لابن منْدَه ( ص (۲۹)، و«الشريعة للآجري (١١٤٨) ، والإبانة الكبرى» لابن بطة (۷۰۹).
And the leader in following, they clarified the paths of guidance, and reached the utmost limit in supporting the religion, and strove to raise the word of Allah without reputation or hypocrisy. And upon those who followed them from the mujtahid imams who compiled the compilations, and established the laws, and derived the rulings of occurrences and events from expression and indication, and implication and requirement, may Allah reward them on my behalf and on behalf of all Muslims with the best reward, especially our greatest Imam, our foremost Imam, the master of the Followers, and the chief of the mujtahids, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, the leader of the people of piety, and upon their followers and imitators, and those who followed their path and adopted their madhhab from the exegetes, hadith scholars, theologians, and jurists. To proceed: The one hoping for the pardon of his Mighty Lord, Abu al-Hasanat Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, may Allah overlook his manifest and hidden sin, the son of the chief of knowledge, the full moon of the virtuous, the sun of the jurists, the crown of the perfect, the vast ocean, the abundant rain, the author of beneficial works, possessing abundant merits and praises, our master al-Hajj al-Hafiz Muhammad Abd al-Halim, may Allah admit him to the abode of bliss and bring him to a noble station: Indeed, it is not hidden from people of intellect that the best of virtues and the most complete of qualities is deep understanding in religion (tafaqquh fi al-din). And to this the master of messengers alluded with his statement which the imams of religion have extracted: 'Whomsoever Allah desires good for, He grants him deep understanding in religion.' And it is the description by which a person distinguishes himself among his peers and likes, and is pointed to in virtue and perfection with fingertips. So blessed is the one who taught it and learned it, and researched it and studied it. Noble books have been authored in the science of fiqh, pure, intermediate and concise, simple and brief. Among the most important intermediate books that include the established principles and branches, upon which the winds of acceptance have blown and the scholars of transmissions have deemed good, is the book 'al-Wiqaya fi Masa'il al-Hidaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a, and its commentary by his student Sadr al-Shari'a, may Allah cool their resting places and sanctify their missions. They attained abundant fame like the fame of the sun at midday. A group of jurists turned their intention to them and wrote commentaries and glosses upon them, and they circulated them among themselves in study and teaching, learning and instructing. But all of them abandoned what was obligatory upon them of mentioning the proofs of rulings and firmly connecting branches to principles. Among them: some abbreviated and were deficient; some lengthened and wearied; you see: some restrict themselves to solving easy points and leave uncovering difficult passages. [Footnote: based on suspicion, and I have detailed the discussion in my treatise 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnat Sayyid al-Abrar' and its annotations called 'Nukhbat al-Ansar'. Ibn Qutlubugha said in Khulasat al-Afkar: al-Daraqutni and Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated it from Ibn Umar, and its meaning has been narrated from Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Anas, and in their chains there is criticism, but they strengthen each other. al-Saghani and al-Tibi declared it hasan. al-Laknawi said in Tuhfat al-Akhyar: It has been narrated with different wordings, and scholars have discussed it in terms of weakening and criticism, until some thought it was fabricated, but it is not so; indeed its chains are weak, but that does not necessitate fabrication. Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghudda said: This hadith is not fabricated. Ibn Hajar said in Talkhis al-Habir: al-Bayhaqi said that the hadith of Muslim conveys some of its meaning, i.e., 'The stars are a security for the sky, when the stars disappear, the sky will be brought what it is promised; I am a security for my Companions, when I go, my Companions will be brought what they are promised; and my Companions are a security for my Ummah, when my Companions go, my Ummah will be brought what they are promised.' See Sahih Muslim, etc.]
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his super-commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya. The author, Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, begins by praising the scholars who followed the Companions and the mujtahid imams, especially his own teacher and father, and then focuses on the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa. He then states that the best virtue is tafaqquh fi al-din (deep understanding of the religion), citing the well-known hadith. He goes on to mention that many books have been written on fiqh, but among the intermediate works, the book 'al-Wiqaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a and its commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a are most famous. However, he criticizes the previous commentators for failing to mention the proofs of rulings and for not properly connecting branches to principles. Some abbreviated, some elongated, and some only solved easy points. The author implies that his own work will remedy these deficiencies. The footnote is a lengthy discussion on the authenticity of a hadith about stars and Companions, citing various scholars and references. The author clarifies that the hadith is not fabricated but has weak chains.

Key Terms
التفقه في الدين (al-tafaqquh fi al-din): Deep understanding and comprehensive knowledge of the religion, especially in matters of rulings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the best virtue?
A) Memorizing hadith
B) Tafaqquh fi al-din
C) Writing commentaries
D) Fasting and prayer

Key Takeaway
Tafaqquh fi al-din is the best virtue, and seeking it is a sign of divine favor.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Fame of al-Wiqaya and Its Commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the book 'al-Wiqaya' and its commentary as central Hanafi texts and describe their acclaim.

Core Idea
Al-Wiqaya and its commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a are among the most famous intermediate Hanafi works.

The author highlights the importance of the book 'al-Wiqaya' and its commentary, praising their acceptance among scholars. This lesson introduces these key texts and their role in Hanafi fiqh study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the books mentioned
Locate the mention of 'al-Wiqaya' and its commentary. Note the authors: Burhan al-Shari'a and Sadr al-Shari'a.
These are standard references in the Hanafi madhhab.
2
Understand the description 'intermediate'
The author classifies these books as 'متوسطة' (intermediate). This means they are between concise and detailed works, containing both principles and branches.
Intermediate texts are ideal for students who have mastered basics.
3
Recognize their fame
The author says they attained fame like the sun at midday. This indicates widespread acceptance and use.
Many commentaries and glosses were written on them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقروم (۱) الاقتداء ، أوضحوا سُبُل الهداية، وبلغوا في نصرة الدين أقصى النهاية ، وجاهدوا في إعلاء كلمةِ الله من غير سُمعة ولا رياء.
وعلى من تبعهم من الأئمة المجتهدين الذين دوّنوا الدواوين، وقتنوا القوانين، واستنبطوا أحكام الوقائع والحوادث من العبارة والإشارة، والدلالة والاقتضاء، جزاهم الله عني وعن سائر المسلمين خير الجزاء، لا سيما على إمامنا الأعظم، وإمامنا الأقدم، سيد التابعين، ورأس المجتهدين ، أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، رئيس أرباب الاتقاء، وعلى مقلديهم ومتبعيهم ، ومن سلك مسلكهم، وتمذهب بمذهبهم من المفسرين والمحدثين والمتكلمين والفقهاء.

And the leader in following, they clarified the paths of guidance, and reached the utmost limit in supporting the religion, and strove to raise the word of Allah without reputation or hypocrisy. And upon those who followed them from the mujtahid imams who compiled the compilations, and established the laws, and derived the rulings of occurrences and events from expression and indication, and implication and requirement, may Allah reward them on my behalf and on behalf of all Muslims with the best reward, especially our greatest Imam, our foremost Imam, the master of the Followers, and the chief of the mujtahids, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, the leader of the people of piety, and upon their followers and imitators, and those who followed their path and adopted their madhhab from the exegetes, hadith scholars, theologians, and jurists. To proceed: The one hoping for the pardon of his Mighty Lord, Abu al-Hasanat Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, may Allah overlook his manifest and hidden sin, the son of the chief of knowledge, the full moon of the virtuous, the sun of the jurists, the crown of the perfect, the vast ocean, the abundant rain, the author of beneficial works, possessing abundant merits and praises, our master al-Hajj al-Hafiz Muhammad Abd al-Halim, may Allah admit him to the abode of bliss and bring him to a noble station: Indeed, it is not hidden from people of intellect that the best of virtues and the most complete of qualities is deep understanding in religion (tafaqquh fi al-din). And to this the master of messengers alluded with his statement which the imams of religion have extracted: 'Whomsoever Allah desires good for, He grants him deep understanding in religion.' And it is the description by which a person distinguishes himself among his peers and likes, and is pointed to in virtue and perfection with fingertips. So blessed is the one who taught it and learned it, and researched it and studied it. Noble books have been authored in the science of fiqh, pure, intermediate and concise, simple and brief. Among the most important intermediate books that include the established principles and branches, upon which the winds of acceptance have blown and the scholars of transmissions have deemed good, is the book 'al-Wiqaya fi Masa'il al-Hidaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a, and its commentary by his student Sadr al-Shari'a, may Allah cool their resting places and sanctify their missions. They attained abundant fame like the fame of the sun at midday. A group of jurists turned their intention to them and wrote commentaries and glosses upon them, and they circulated them among themselves in study and teaching, learning and instructing. But all of them abandoned what was obligatory upon them of mentioning the proofs of rulings and firmly connecting branches to principles. Among them: some abbreviated and were deficient; some lengthened and wearied; you see: some restrict themselves to solving easy points and leave uncovering difficult passages. [Footnote: based on suspicion, and I have detailed the discussion in my treatise 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnat Sayyid al-Abrar' and its annotations called 'Nukhbat al-Ansar'. Ibn Qutlubugha said in Khulasat al-Afkar: al-Daraqutni and Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated it from Ibn Umar, and its meaning has been narrated from Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Anas, and in their chains there is criticism, but they strengthen each other. al-Saghani and al-Tibi declared it hasan. al-Laknawi said in Tuhfat al-Akhyar: It has been narrated with different wordings, and scholars have discussed it in terms of weakening and criticism, until some thought it was fabricated, but it is not so; indeed its chains are weak, but that does not necessitate fabrication. Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghudda said: This hadith is not fabricated. Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his super-commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya. The author, Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, begins by praising the scholars who followed the Companions and the mujtahid imams, especially his own teacher and father, and then focuses on the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa. He then states that the best virtue is tafaqquh fi al-din (deep understanding of the religion), citing the well-known hadith. He goes on to mention that many books have been written on fiqh, but among the intermediate works, the book 'al-Wiqaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a and its commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a are most famous. However, he criticizes the previous commentators for failing to mention the proofs of rulings and for not properly connecting branches to principles. Some abbreviated, some elongated, and some only solved easy points. The author implies that his own work will remedy these deficiencies. The footnote is a lengthy discussion on the authenticity of a hadith about stars and Companions, citing various scholars and references. The author clarifies that the hadith is not fabricated but has weak chains.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqaya): A famous Hanafi fiqh text by Burhan al-Shari'a, a matn (text) on rulings
برهان الشريعة (Burhan al-Shari'a): Title of the author of al-Wiqaya, meaning 'Proof of the Shari'a'; his name is Mahmud ibn Ahmad
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'a): Title of the commentator of al-Wiqaya, meaning 'Chief of the Shari'a'; his name is Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of 'al-Wiqaya' and its commentary according to the author?
A) They are unknown works.
B) They are among the most famous intermediate books on fiqh.
C) They are beginner-level texts.
D) They are only for advanced scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Wiqaya and its commentary are central intermediate Hanafi texts, widely accepted and studied.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Author's Criticique of Previous Commentators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two flaws the author finds in previous commentaries on al-Wiqaya and explain his proposed remedy.

Core Idea
Previous commentators failed to mention proofs and connect branches to principles, leading to incomplete works.

After praising the texts, the author points out a serious deficiency in existing commentaries. This lesson examines his criticism and what he aims to correct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deficiency
Find where the author says previous commentators 'abandoned what was obligatory': mentioning proofs and connecting branches to principles.
This is a methodological critique.
2
Categorize the types of commentators
He divides them into two groups: those who abbreviated (اقتصر فأخل) and those who lengthened (طول فأمل). Understand what each group lacked.
The first group omitted essentials; the second group wearied readers without clarity.
3
Understand the author's goal
The author implies that his own commentary will remedy this by providing proofs and proper connections.
This sets the stage for the rest of his work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقروم (۱) الاقتداء ، أوضحوا سُبُل الهداية، وبلغوا في نصرة الدين أقصى النهاية ، وجاهدوا في إعلاء كلمةِ الله من غير سُمعة ولا رياء.
وعلى من تبعهم من الأئمة المجتهدين الذين دوّنوا الدواوين، وقتنوا القوانين، واستنبطوا أحكام الوقائع والحوادث من العبارة والإشارة، والدلالة والاقتضاء، جزاهم الله عني وعن سائر المسلمين خير الجزاء، لا سيما على إمامنا الأعظم، وإمامنا الأقدم، سيد التابعين، ورأس المجتهدين ، أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، رئيس أرباب الاتقاء، وعلى مقلديهم ومتبعيهم ، ومن سلك مسلكهم، وتمذهب بمذهبهم من المفسرين والمحدثين والمتكلمين والفقهاء.
أما بعد :
فيقول الراجي عفو ربِّه القوي، أبو الحسنات محمد عبد الحي اللكهنوي (۲) تجاوز الله عن ذنبه الجلي والخفي، ابن صدر العلم، بدر الفضلاء، شمس الفقهاء، تاج الكملاء، البحر الزخار الغيث المدرار، صاحب التصانيف النافعة، ذي المناقب والمحامد الوافرة، مولانا الحاج الحافظ محمد عبد الحليم ) ، أدخله الله دار النعيم، وأوصله إلى مقام كريم : إنه لا يخفى على أرباب النهي أن أفضل الفضائل وأكمل الشمائل هو التفقه في الدين، وإليه أشار سيد المرسلين، بقوله الذي أخرجته أئمة الدين: «من يُرد الله به خيراً يفقهه في الدين (۲) وهو الوصف الذي يمتاز به المرء بين الأقران والأماثل، ويكون مشاراً إليه في الفضل والكمال بالأنامل ، فطوبى لمن عَلَّمَه وتعلمه، وباحث فيه ودرسه. وقد صُنفت في علم الفقه كتب شريفة، وزُيرٌ ،نظيفة، وسيطة ووجيزة، وبسيطة وقصيرة، ومن أجل الكتب المتوسطة المشتملة على الأصول والفروع المعتبرة، التي هبت عليها رياح القبول، واستحسنها علماء النقول ، كتاب «الوقاية في مسائل الهداية» لبرهان الشريعة، وشرحها لتلميذه صدر الشريعة، برَّدَ اللهُ مضجعهما، وقدَّسَ اللهُ مبعثهما ، وقد نالا حظاً وافراً من الاشتهار لا كاشتهار الشمس على نصف النهار. وقد صرف جمع من الفقهاء عنان عزيمتهما إليهما فكتبوا شروحاً وتعليقات عليهما، وتداولوهما فيما بينهم درساً وتدريساً وتعلماً وتعليماً، وقد تركوا كلهم ما هو الواجب عليهم من ذكر أدلة الأحكام، وربط الفروع بالأصول بالإحكام :
فمنهم : من اقتصر فأخل.
ومنهم : مَن طول فأمل، ترى :
بعضهم : يكتفون على حل المواضع السهلة، ويتركون كشف المقامات المغلقة.
على ما ظنّ، وقد فصلت الكلام فيه في رسالتي «تحفة الأخيار في إحياء سنة سيد الأبرار» (٥٣ - ٦٥) ، وتعليقاتها المسماة بـ «نخبة الأنظار » (ص ٥٣ - ٦٥ ، فلتطالع منه رحمه الله تعالى. وقال ابن قطلوبغا الله في خلاصة الأفكار ( ص ٥٨) : رواه الدارقطني وابن عبد البر من حديث ابن عمر الله ، وقد رُوي معناه من حديث عمر ، ومن حديث ابن عباس ه ، ومن حديث أنس له ، وفي أسانيدهما مقال، لكن يشد بعضها بعضا». وحسنه الصغاني والطيبي، قال اللكنوي في تحفة الأخيار» (ص ٥٣ ) : روي ذلك بألفاظ مختلفة، وقد طال كلامهم على هذا الحديث تضعيفاً وجرحاً، حتى ظن بعضهم أنه حديث موضوع، وليس كذلك، نعم طرق روايته ضعيفة، ولا يلزم منه وضعها». وقال الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة في تعليقاته على تحفة الأخيار» (ص) ٥٤) : ورد هذا الحديث في الجملة وأنه ليس بموضوع». وقال ابن حجر في تلخيص الحبير» (٤) : ١٩١) : «ذكر عن البيهقي أنه قال : إن حديث مسلم يؤدّي بعض معناه ، يعني قوله : «النجوم أمنة للسماء ، فإذا ذهبن النجوم أتى السماء ما توعد، وأنا أمنة لأصحابي ، فإذا ذهبت أتى أصحابي ما يوعدون، وأصحابي أمنة لأمتي، فإذا ذهب أصحابي أتى أمتي ما يوعدون.» في صحيح مسلم ٤ : ١٩٦١ ، وصحيح ابن حبان ١٦ : ٢٣٤ ، و(مسند أحمد ٤ : ۳۹۸ ، وغيرها. وينظر : تعليق السيد عبد الله الغماري على تأييد الحقيقة العلية للسيوطي » ( ص ٩٦) ، و (خلاصة البدر المنير لابن الملقن (۲ : ٤۳۱ ) ، وكشف الخفاء» (۱) : (١٤٧) ، و (لسان الميزان (۲) : (۱۳۷)، و«الفوائد» لابن منْدَه ( ص (۲۹)، و«الشريعة للآجري (١١٤٨) ، والإبانة الكبرى» لابن بطة (۷۰۹).
And the leader in following, they clarified the paths of guidance, and reached the utmost limit in supporting the religion, and strove to raise the word of Allah without reputation or hypocrisy. And upon those who followed them from the mujtahid imams who compiled the compilations, and established the laws, and derived the rulings of occurrences and events from expression and indication, and implication and requirement, may Allah reward them on my behalf and on behalf of all Muslims with the best reward, especially our greatest Imam, our foremost Imam, the master of the Followers, and the chief of the mujtahids, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, the leader of the people of piety, and upon their followers and imitators, and those who followed their path and adopted their madhhab from the exegetes, hadith scholars, theologians, and jurists. To proceed: The one hoping for the pardon of his Mighty Lord, Abu al-Hasanat Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, may Allah overlook his manifest and hidden sin, the son of the chief of knowledge, the full moon of the virtuous, the sun of the jurists, the crown of the perfect, the vast ocean, the abundant rain, the author of beneficial works, possessing abundant merits and praises, our master al-Hajj al-Hafiz Muhammad Abd al-Halim, may Allah admit him to the abode of bliss and bring him to a noble station: Indeed, it is not hidden from people of intellect that the best of virtues and the most complete of qualities is deep understanding in religion (tafaqquh fi al-din). And to this the master of messengers alluded with his statement which the imams of religion have extracted: 'Whomsoever Allah desires good for, He grants him deep understanding in religion.' And it is the description by which a person distinguishes himself among his peers and likes, and is pointed to in virtue and perfection with fingertips. So blessed is the one who taught it and learned it, and researched it and studied it. Noble books have been authored in the science of fiqh, pure, intermediate and concise, simple and brief. Among the most important intermediate books that include the established principles and branches, upon which the winds of acceptance have blown and the scholars of transmissions have deemed good, is the book 'al-Wiqaya fi Masa'il al-Hidaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a, and its commentary by his student Sadr al-Shari'a, may Allah cool their resting places and sanctify their missions. They attained abundant fame like the fame of the sun at midday. A group of jurists turned their intention to them and wrote commentaries and glosses upon them, and they circulated them among themselves in study and teaching, learning and instructing. But all of them abandoned what was obligatory upon them of mentioning the proofs of rulings and firmly connecting branches to principles. Among them: some abbreviated and were deficient; some lengthened and wearied; you see: some restrict themselves to solving easy points and leave uncovering difficult passages. [Footnote: based on suspicion, and I have detailed the discussion in my treatise 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnat Sayyid al-Abrar' and its annotations called 'Nukhbat al-Ansar'. Ibn Qutlubugha said in Khulasat al-Afkar: al-Daraqutni and Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated it from Ibn Umar, and its meaning has been narrated from Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Anas, and in their chains there is criticism, but they strengthen each other. al-Saghani and al-Tibi declared it hasan. al-Laknawi said in Tuhfat al-Akhyar: It has been narrated with different wordings, and scholars have discussed it in terms of weakening and criticism, until some thought it was fabricated, but it is not so; indeed its chains are weak, but that does not necessitate fabrication. Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghudda said: This hadith is not fabricated. Ibn Hajar said in Talkhis al-Habir: al-Bayhaqi said that the hadith of Muslim conveys some of its meaning, i.e., 'The stars are a security for the sky, when the stars disappear, the sky will be brought what it is promised; I am a security for my Companions, when I go, my Companions will be brought what they are promised; and my Companions are a security for my Ummah, when my Companions go, my Ummah will be brought what they are promised.' See Sahih Muslim, etc.]
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his super-commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya. The author, Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, begins by praising the scholars who followed the Companions and the mujtahid imams, especially his own teacher and father, and then focuses on the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa. He then states that the best virtue is tafaqquh fi al-din (deep understanding of the religion), citing the well-known hadith. He goes on to mention that many books have been written on fiqh, but among the intermediate works, the book 'al-Wiqaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a and its commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a are most famous. However, he criticizes the previous commentators for failing to mention the proofs of rulings and for not properly connecting branches to principles. Some abbreviated, some elongated, and some only solved easy points. The author implies that his own work will remedy these deficiencies. The footnote is a lengthy discussion on the authenticity of a hadith about stars and Companions, citing various scholars and references. The author clarifies that the hadith is not fabricated but has weak chains.

Key Terms
الأدلة (al-adilla): Proofs or evidence that establish a ruling, such as Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
الفروع (al-furu): Branches; specific rulings derived from principles.
الأصول (al-usul): Principles; the foundations of fiqh, also refers to the science of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what did previous commentaries on al-Wiqaya fail to do?
A) They did not include Arabic grammar.
B) They omitted mentioning proofs and connecting branches to principles.
C) They were too short.
D) They focused only on difficult points.

Key Takeaway
Previous commentaries on al-Wiqaya failed to provide evidence and connect rulings to principles, a deficiency the author aims to correct.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Footnote: Authenticity of the Hadith of Stars and Companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the authenticity of the hadith about stars and Companions based on the scholars cited in the footnote.

Core Idea
The hadith about stars and Companions is not fabricated, though its chains are weak; it is strengthened by corroboration.

The author includes a lengthy footnote on the hadith about stars being a security for the sky and Companions for the Ummah. This lesson analyzes the discussion on its authenticity, showing scholarly method in hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith in question
The hadith is: 'The stars are a security for the sky...' and continues with the Prophet as security for his Companions, and Companions for the Ummah.
This hadith appears in Sahih Muslim and other collections.
2
Understand the criticism
Some scholars considered it weak or even fabricated because of weak individual chains. Note that al-Laknawi clarifies it is not fabricated.
The chains are weak but not a fabrication (wad').
3
See the basis for acceptance
The hadith is accepted because multiple weak chains strengthen each other (yashudd ba'duha ba'da). Also, it is supported by similar meanings in authentic hadith.
Principles: corroboration (i'tibar) and external support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقروم (۱) الاقتداء ، أوضحوا سُبُل الهداية، وبلغوا في نصرة الدين أقصى النهاية ، وجاهدوا في إعلاء كلمةِ الله من غير سُمعة ولا رياء.
وعلى من تبعهم من الأئمة المجتهدين الذين دوّنوا الدواوين، وقتنوا القوانين، واستنبطوا أحكام الوقائع والحوادث من العبارة والإشارة، والدلالة والاقتضاء، جزاهم الله عني وعن سائر المسلمين خير الجزاء، لا سيما على إمامنا الأعظم، وإمامنا الأقدم، سيد التابعين، ورأس المجتهدين ، أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، رئيس أرباب الاتقاء، وعلى مقلديهم ومتبعيهم ، ومن سلك مسلكهم، وتمذهب بمذهبهم من المفسرين والمحدثين والمتكلمين والفقهاء.

And the leader in following, they clarified the paths of guidance, and reached the utmost limit in supporting the religion, and strove to raise the word of Allah without reputation or hypocrisy. And upon those who followed them from the mujtahid imams who compiled the compilations, and established the laws, and derived the rulings of occurrences and events from expression and indication, and implication and requirement, may Allah reward them on my behalf and on behalf of all Muslims with the best reward, especially our greatest Imam, our foremost Imam, the master of the Followers, and the chief of the mujtahids, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, the leader of the people of piety, and upon their followers and imitators, and those who followed their path and adopted their madhhab from the exegetes, hadith scholars, theologians, and jurists. They attained abundant fame like the fame of the sun at midday. A group of jurists turned their intention to them and wrote commentaries and glosses upon them, and they circulated them among themselves in study and teaching, learning and instructing. But all of them abandoned what was obligatory upon them of mentioning the proofs of rulings and firmly connecting branches to principles. Among them: some abbreviated and were deficient; some lengthened and wearied; you see: some restrict themselves to solving easy points and leave uncovering difficult passages. [Footnote: based on suspicion, and I have detailed the discussion in my treatise 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnat Sayyid al-Abrar' and its annotations called 'Nukhbat al-Ansar'. Ibn Qutlubugha said in Khulasat al-Afkar: al-Daraqutni and Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated it from Ibn Umar, and its meaning has been narrated from Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Anas, and in their chains there is criticism, but they strengthen each other. al-Saghani and al-Tibi declared it hasan. al-Laknawi said in Tuhfat al-Akhyar: It has been narrated with different wordings, and scholars have discussed it in terms of weakening and criticism, until some thought it was fabricated, but it is not so; indeed its chains are weak, but that does not necessitate fabrication. Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghudda said: This hadith is not fabricated. Ibn Hajar said in Talkhis al-Habir: al-Bayhaqi said that the hadith of Muslim conveys some of its meaning, i.e., 'The stars are a security for the sky, when the stars disappear, the sky will be brought what it is promised; I am a security for my Companions, when I go, my Companions will be brought what they are promised; and my Companions are a security for my Ummah, when my Companions go, my Ummah will be brought what they are promised.' See Sahih Muslim, etc.]
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his super-commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya. The author, Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, begins by praising the scholars who followed the Companions and the mujtahid imams, especially his own teacher and father, and then focuses on the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa. He then states that the best virtue is tafaqquh fi al-din (deep understanding of the religion), citing the well-known hadith. He goes on to mention that many books have been written on fiqh, but among the intermediate works, the book 'al-Wiqaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a and its commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a are most famous. However, he criticizes the previous commentators for failing to mention the proofs of rulings and for not properly connecting branches to principles. Some abbreviated, some elongated, and some only solved easy points. The author implies that his own work will remedy these deficiencies. The footnote is a lengthy discussion on the authenticity of a hadith about stars and Companions, citing various scholars and references. The author clarifies that the hadith is not fabricated but has weak chains.

Key Terms
حديث موضوع (hadith mawdu'): A fabricated hadith, falsely attributed to the Prophet.
يشد بعضها بعضا (yashudd ba'duha ba'da): One narration strengthens another; a principle in hadith criticism where multiple weak chains gain strength through corroboration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is al-Laknawi's final position on the hadith about stars and Companions?
A) It is fabricated.
B) It is authentic without doubt.
C) It is not fabricated, though its chains are weak.
D) It is weak and cannot be used.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of stars and Companions is not fabricated; its weak chains are strengthened by corroboration and supporting evidence.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Author's Preface: Laying the Foundation for Proof-Based Fiqh
Author's preface outlining the virtue of tafaqquh and the need for proofs in fiqh commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam al-Laknawi criticized earlier commentators and describe his own methodology of linking furu' to usul with proofs.

Core Idea
A Hanafi commentary must prove every ruling — linking branches to principles is obligatory, not optional.

This preface is more than a mere introduction; it is a manifesto for a rigorous fiqh methodology. Al-Laknawi lauds the virtue of tafaqquh, praises al-Wiqaya and its commentary, but then sharply criticizes earlier glossators for neglecting the essential duty of citing evidences and connecting branches to principles. He then traces his own scholarly evolution from a brief student gloss to the comprehensive proof-laden al-Si'aya and finally to the concise Umdat al-Ri'aya. Understanding this preface gives us insight into what a proper Hanafi commentary should achieve.

Guided Path
1
Identify the virtue being extolled
What is the best virtue according to the hadith cited? (tafaqquh – deep understanding in religion)
Al-Laknawi opens by emphasizing tafaqquh as the highest virtue.
2
Recognize the praise of al-Wiqaya and its commentary
Why does al-Laknawi praise these works? They are distinguished intermediate texts that encompass principles and branches.
He acknowledges their fame and acceptance among scholars.
3
Analyze the criticism of earlier commentators
What did they neglect? The obligatory task of mentioning proofs (adilla) and linking branches to principles.
Some were brief, some verbose, but all failed in this duty.
4
Trace the author's scholarly journey
From a short gloss under his father → large commentary al-Si'aya → concise Umdat al-Ri'aya. What motivated each step?
The short gloss was insufficient; al-Si'aya aimed to prove rulings; Umdat al-Ri'aya was a condensed request from friends.
5
Understand the defense of the title 'al-Si'aya'
Some objected that 'Si'aya' means slander. How does al-Laknawi refute this? He cites usage in fiqh and language meaning 'effort'.
This shows his attention to precision and defending his work.

6
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, the Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, his family, and all his companions.
The preface of Imam al-Laknawi.
[Allah forgive his manifest and hidden sin,] Ibn Sadr al-Ilm, Badr al-Fudala, Shams al-Fuqaha', Taj al-Kumala, the overflowing sea, the abundant rain, the author of beneficial works, possessor of ample virtues and praises, our master al-Hajj al-Hafiz Muhammad Abd al-Halim—may Allah admit him to the Abode of Bliss and lead him to a noble station. Indeed, it is not hidden from people of intellect that the best of virtues and the most complete of characteristics is deep understanding (tafaqquh) in religion. The Master of Messengers pointed to this in his statement, which the Imams of religion have narrated: 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He grants him deep understanding in religion.' It is the quality by which a person is distinguished among his peers and equals, and by which he is pointed out for virtue and perfection by fingers. So blessed is the one who teaches it, learns it, researches it, and studies it. Noble books have been authored in the science of fiqh, both medium and concise, extensive and brief. Among the most distinguished intermediate books that encompass accepted principles and branches, upon which the winds of acceptance have blown and which scholars of transmitted knowledge have deemed excellent, is the book 'al-Wiqaya fi Masa'il al-Hidaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a, and its commentary by his student Sadr al-Shari'a—may Allah cool their resting places and sanctify their resurrection. They have achieved abundant fame, not less than the fame of the sun at midday. A group of jurists have turned their resolve toward them, writing commentaries and glosses on them, and they have circulated them among themselves for study, teaching, learning, and instruction. Yet, all of them have neglected what was obligatory upon them: mentioning the proofs of rulings and firmly linking the branches to the principles. Among them: some were brief and deficient; some were lengthy and verbose. You see: some suffice with solving easy places and leave uncovering difficult positions. Some multiply by presenting questions and answers. Some lengthen by presenting juristic branches. 
When I was reading 'Sharh al-Wiqaya' in the presence of my honored father, the all-knowing scholar—may Allah admit him to the Abode of Peace—I wrote a gloss upon it by his noble command, encompassing the solution of some positions according to his lofty exposition. Then, when my state advanced and I rose from the lowest to the peak of perfection, I saw that it (the gloss) did not suffice its student due to its brevity, nor benefit the complete ones due to its conciseness. So I commenced a large commentary named 'al-Si'aya fi Kashf ma fi Sharh al-Wiqaya', in which I undertook to stud the issues with proofs, establish transmitted knowledge with rational knowledge, and tie the branches to the principles, while mentioning the differences of the Companions, the Followers, and the mujtahids after them, and presenting their proofs according to their methodology, with refutation and confirmation, criticism and authentication, on the condition of fairness without bigotry or oppression. I hope from Allah the Generous, who has granted us success for this great matter, that He extend my life, complete my affair, perfect my commentary, achieve my aim, and make it a means for the benefit of His servants and a reforming judgment in disputes among His servants. 
Then some of my sincere friends and eminent companions requested that I write a gloss (hashiya) on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya' and compose a brief commentary from 'al-Si'aya'. So I hastened to fulfill their request and achieve their proposal, thinking that the book 'al-Si'aya', due to its comprehensiveness, would take a long time to complete, and hastening to spread knowledge as much as possible is better than delaying it. So I wrote a commentary on it and named it 'Umdat al-Ri'aya fi Hall Sharh al-Wiqaya'. 
(1) He wrote this brief commentary while reading 'Sharh al-Wiqaya' to his noble father at the end of the tenth decade of the second millennium after the Hijra—may the best prayers and purest greetings be upon its owner. He wrote, by his father's noble command, a brief gloss on some places, preceding step by step, encompassing the solution of some positions sporadically, and its name was 'Husn al-Wilaya bi-Hall Sharh al-Wiqaya', which covers the first half of 'Sharh al-Wiqaya'. See: 'al-Si'aya' (1: 2-3) and 'al-Manhaj al-Fiqhi li'l-Imam al-Laknawi' (p. 465). (2) I heard that some people of the time objected to my naming my commentary 'al-Si'aya', saying that 'al-Si'aya' in language means slander. This is strange from him, indicating his ignorance of the language and the books of Shari'a, for the books of fiqh and hadith are unanimous in using this word in the sense of 'saiy' (effort), as is not hidden from one who has perused the chapters of emancipation, the contract of writing (mukataba), bequests, and others. In the 'Dala'il' regarding the descriptions of the Prophet (peace be upon him), he is specifically honored with the honor of 'si'aya', and in books of language it is said: 'sa'a sa'yan wa si'ayatan.' From him, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya', a commentary on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya'. Imam al-Laknawi begins by extolling the virtue of tafaqquh (deep understanding) in religion, citing the well-known hadith from Bukhari and Muslim that whoever Allah intends good for, He grants them understanding of religion. He then praises the book 'al-Wiqaya' by Burhan al-Shari'a and its commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a, noting their fame and acceptance among scholars. However, he criticizes previous commentators for failing to adequately mention the proofs (adilla) of rulings and for not properly connecting furu' (branches) to usul (principles). He describes that some were too brief, some too verbose, some only solved easy issues, and some focused on questions and answers or on listing branches without proofs. 
Al-Laknawi then narrates his own scholarly journey. Initially, he wrote a short gloss on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya' under his father's supervision, but later felt it was too brief. So he authored a large commentary called 'al-Si'aya', which aimed to link each ruling with its evidence, combine transmitted knowledge with rational reasoning, and include the differences of early authorities. He promised fairness and lack of bias. Then, at the request of friends, he produced a more concise gloss from 'al-Si'aya', which he named 'Umdat al-Ri'aya fi Hall Sharh al-Wiqaya'. 
The author also includes a footnote defending the name 'al-Si'aya' against those who misunderstood it as slander, clarifying that in fiqh contexts it means effort or endeavor. This preface sets the stage for the work's methodology: a focus on proofs (adilla) and the systematic connection of branches to principles, which is a hallmark of the Hanafi usul approach.

Key Terms
التفقه (al-tafaqquh): Deep understanding in religion, specifically the study and comprehension of fiqh (jurisprudence). Here, it is presented as the best virtue and a sign of Allah's intention for good.
الوقاية (al-Wiqaya): A famous work by Burhan al-Shari'a, titled 'al-Wiqaya fi Masa'il al-Hidaya', which is an abridgment of 'al-Hidaya'. It is a standard Hanafi text on furu' al-fiqh.
السعاية (al-Si'aya): The large commentary by Imam al-Laknawi on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya', in which he intended to thoroughly cite proofs and connect branches to principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of al-Laknawi's large commentary 'al-Si'aya'?
A) To provide a brief gloss on difficult points
B) To link each ruling with its evidence and connect branches to principles
C) To enumerate all the branches of fiqh without proofs
D) To criticize the works of Burhan al-Shari'a and Sadr al-Shari'a

Key Takeaway
Al-Laknawi's preface establishes that a proper fiqh commentary must do more than explain words—it must prove each ruling by linking branches to principles with evidences.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Al-Lakhnawi's Method and Six Commitments
Author's introduction and methodological statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six scholarly commitments al-Lakhnawi makes in his introduction and explain how they reflect Hanafi values of proof-based analysis and sincere intention.

Core Idea
Six commitments: proofs, principles, intra-Hanafi focus, critique, fairness, and sincere intention for the Hereafter.

This introduction reveals the scholarly personality of Imam Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi as he sets out his method for writing 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah'. Understanding his six commitments gives you a window into how a Hanafi commentator balances tradition, criticism, and personal sincerity. You will see how he views his work as both a service to students and a provision for his own afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's initial motivation
Note how al-Lakhnawi began writing a brief gloss at his father's command while studying 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'. Later he felt it was too brief and composed a larger work 'al-Sa'ayah' before extracting the current book.
This shows the chain of commentary within the Hanafi tradition: from matn to sharh to hashiya.
2
List the six methodological commitments
From the numbered section of the introduction, extract each commitment: (1) solving matn and sharh with jarh and daf', (2) citing evidences from Quran, Sunnah, Companions, and usul, (3) focusing on Hanafi differences only, (4) detailed clarification of questions and answers, (5) including needed subsidiary issues, (6) refuting doubts on Hanafi issues.
Commitment 3 is key: he deliberately ignores non-Hanafi differences to avoid digression.
3
Analyze the purpose of criticism (jarh) as used here
Al-Lakhnawi uses 'jarh' technically to mean scholarly evaluation, not disrespect. He pairs it with 'daf'' (defense). This reflects the Hanafi usul method of engaging with objections fairly.
Misunderstanding this term can lead to accusations of disrespect.
4
Understand the defense of the title 'al-Sa'ayah'
The author responds to critics who mistook the word for 'slander'. He demonstrates lexical and hadith-based evidence that 'sa'ayah' here means 'effort', consistent with Islamic legal terminology.
This shows the importance of precise terminological knowledge in Hanafi scholarship.
5
Reflect on the author's stated intention
Al-Lakhnawi explicitly denies worldly motives (riya', sum'ah, iftikhār). He frames his work as provision for the Hereafter and benefit for students, citing Taj al-Subki's poetry about the sweetness of scholarly labor.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on ikhlas (sincerity) in religious works.
