The First Study: The Spread of Knowledge. Al-Jami', Abu Muti' al-Balkhi, Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti, and others. Then the opponents acknowledged his superiority and conceded to him all sciences, until Imam Malik said when asked about Abu Hanifa: 'I saw him as a man who, if he spoke to you about this pillar being gold, would argue convincingly.' He also said: 'Abu Hanifa is the best companion for the people of fiqh.' And al-Shafi'i said: 'All people are dependent on Abu Hanifa in fiqh.' So our Hanafi companions, may Allah treat them with hidden kindness, are the foremost in fiqh and ijtihad, and they have the highest rank in opinion and hadith. He also said: 'Indeed, many of our companions dispersed in villages and cities: among them are our early companions in Iraq such as Baghdad, for it is the seat of the caliphate and the house of knowledge and guidance. And among them are the mashayikh of Balkh in Khurasan, and the mashayikh of Samarkand, and the mashayikh of Bukhara. And among them are mashayikh from other lands such as Rayy, Shiraz, Tus, Zinjan, Hamadan, Astarabad, Bastam, Marghinan, Farghana, Damghan, and other cities in the region of Transoxiana, Khurasan, Azerbaijan, Mazandaran, Khwarazm, Ghazna, Kirman up to the land of India, and all of Transoxiana and other cities of Arab Iraq and Persian Iraq. They spread the knowledge of Abu Hanifa through dictation, reminders, and compositions, and people of all classes benefited from them, so the number of jurists became incalculable, and their dictations and compositions are beyond counting or enumeration. They would study fiqh, exert ijtihad, benefit, answer real events, compose original works, give fatwas on unprecedented cases, and compile issues. Thus the order of the world remained, and the arrangement of its people was upon the best system, and its prosperity continued through the cycles of nights and days until Allah decreed the emergence of Genghis Khan, who wielded the sword, killed people, destroyed inhabited areas, annihilated cities, and moved among them like a razor on hair and attacked them like locusts on green crops. He advanced on Khwarazm and ravaged it, killed its sultan Khwarazm Shah Muhammad and obliterated it. Shaykh Najm al-Din al-Kubra was granted martyrdom in this great calamity at the hand of this infidel, sinful, tyrannical group in the year 616 AH. Then his sons and followers succeeded him and emphasized his actions until Hulagu the infidel son of Genghis the sinful entered Baghdad with a huge army in the time of Caliph al-Musta'sim, the last of the Abbasid caliphs, in the year 656 AH. He descended upon Baghdad, killed the caliph, and the army of the infidel Tatars attacked the house of the caliphate and killed those in Baghdad among the jurists. The Hanafi jurists in those lands were few, so they moved with their families to Damascus and Aleppo. Those lands were at that time in good order, and jurists came to them from other lands and students from every place, until the oppression of the Circassian sultans occurred there, and the conditions of order became reversed, so knowledge and its people migrated to other lands.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a historical account of the spread of the Hanafi school of law and its subsequent devastation by the Mongol invasions. The author begins by recounting the praise of Imam Abu Hanifa by the great imams of other schools: Imam Malik said that Abu Hanifa could argue convincingly even for an improbable claim, and that Abu Hanifa is the best companion for the people of fiqh. Imam al-Shafi'i declared that all people are dependent on Abu Hanifa in fiqh. This establishes the superiority and centrality of the Hanafi school. The text then describes the geographic expansion of Hanafi scholars across the Islamic world, including Iraq, Khurasan, Transoxiana, India, and beyond. These scholars spread the knowledge of Abu Hanifa through teaching, writing, and issuing fatwas on new occurrences (nawazil). Their activity is presented as the reason for the order and prosperity of the world. The turning point comes with the rise of Genghis Khan and the Mongol invasions. The author describes the devastation in detail: the Mongols killed people, destroyed cities, and moved like a razor or locusts. The first major blow was against Khwarazm in 616 AH, where the Sufi shaykh Najm al-Din al-Kubra was martyred. Then Hulagu completed the destruction by sacking Baghdad in 656 AH, killing the caliph and many jurists. Hanafi jurists, being few in those lands, fled to Damascus and Aleppo. However, later oppression by the Circassian sultans caused further decline, forcing scholars to migrate again. The passage serves to contextualize the challenges faced by the Hanafi school and the resilience of its scholars in preserving and transmitting knowledge despite immense hardships.

Key Terms
شيوع العلم (shuyūʿ al-ʿilm): The spread of knowledge, referring to the dissemination of Hanafi fiqh across various regions.
نوازل (nawāzil): Unprecedented legal cases or events requiring new fatwas.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): Independent legal reasoning to derive rulings from primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What did Imam Malik say about Imam Abu Hanifa when asked about him?
A) He said Abu Hanifa is the best companion for the people of fiqh.
B) He said all people are dependent on Abu Hanifa in fiqh.
C) He said Abu Hanifa was not a real jurist.
D) He said Abu Hanifa's knowledge was limited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's pre-Mongol expansion was vast, but its scholarly centers were devastated, leading to migration and survival through adaptation.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Defining the Third Layer: Ashab al-Takhrij
Definition of third layer jurists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the role and limitations of ashab al-takhrij within the Hanafi school hierarchy.

Core Idea
Ashab al-takhrij are muqallids who can derive rulings for unstated cases but cannot oppose the school's principles.

The Hanafi school is stratified by ijtihad ability. The third layer, ashab al-takhrij, occupy a middle ground: they are muqallids but possess limited ijtihad to resolve ambiguities. This lesson unpacks their precise role as described in classical works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the layer
Locate the phrase 'طبقة أصحاب التخريج' and note that they are classified as 'المقلدين'.
2
Define takhrij
Explain that takhrij means deriving rulings for cases without explicit narrations, using school principles and analogy.
Takhrij is distinct from independent ijtihad.
3
Understand their ability
They can exercise ijtihad on matters where no transmitted text exists ('في المسائل التي لا رواية فيها').
4
Understand their limitation
They cannot contradict the school in either subsidiary rulings (furu') or principles (usul).
This distinguishes them from higher-ranked mujtahids.
5
Note the practical utility
Their work involves detailing ambiguous statements transmitted from the founders by analogical reasoning.
Example: takhrij al-Razi in al-Hidayah.

الدراسة الثانية: طبقات الحنفية
الثالثة : طبقة أصحاب التخريج . المقلدين ؛ كالرازي وغيره من طبقة من يقدر على الاجتهاد في المسائل التي لا رواية فيها، ولا يقدر على مخالفة صاحب المذهب لا في الفروع، ولا في الأصول، وهو منظور فيه ؛ فإنَّ له درجة عالية، ورتبة شامخة، قد خالف بها صاحب المذهب في كثير من الأصول والفروع، ومن طالع «شرح معاني الآثار»، وغيره من مصنفاته يجده يختار خلاف ما اختارَهُ صاحب المذهب كثيراً ، إذا كان ما يدل عليه قوياً. فالحق أنه من المجتهدين المنتسبين الذين ينتسبون إلى إمام معين من المجتهدين ، لكن لا يقلدونه لا في الفروع ، ولا في الأصول، لكونهم متصفين بالاجتهاد، وما انتسبوا إليه إلا لسلوكهم طريقه في الاجتهاد. وإن انحط عن ذلك، فهو من المجتهدين في المذهب القادرين على استخراج الأحكام من القواعد التي قررها الإمام، ولا تنحط مرتبته عن هذه المرتبة أبدا على رغم أنف من جعلهُ منحطاً، وما أحسن كلام المولى عبد العزيز المحدّث الدَّهْلَوِيّ في «بستان المحدِّثِينَ»، حيث قال ما معربه : إِنَّ «مختصر الطحاوي) يدلُّ على أنه كان مجتهداً ، ولم يكن مقلداً للمذهب الحنفي تقليداً محضاً، فإنه اختار فيه أشياء تخالف مذهب أبي حنيفة لما لاح له من الأدلة القوية. انتهى. وفي الجملة فهو في طبقة أبي يوسف ومحمد ، لا ينحط عن مرتبتهما على القول المسدَّدِ». وأضرابه). عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية فإنهم لا يقدرون على الاجتهاد أصلاً ، لكنّهم لإحاطتهم بالأصول، وضبطهم للمأخذ يقدرون على تفصيل قول مجمل ذي وجهين، وحكم مبهم محتمل لأمرين ، منقول عن أبي حنيفة أو عن واحد من أصحابه، بنظرهم ورأيهم في الأصول، والمقايسة على أمثاله ونظائره من الفروع ، وما وقع في «الهداية» كذا في تخريج الرازي من هذا القبيل.
The study of the layers of Hanafis. (Thirdly:) The layer of the people of takhrij, the muqallids, like al-Razi and others of the layer who are able to exercise ijtihad in matters for which there is no narration, but they are not able to oppose the imam of the school neither in branches nor in principles. And he is looked into: for he has a high rank and lofty station, by which he has opposed the imam in many principles and branches. Whoever looks at 'Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar' and other works will find him often choosing contrary to what the imam chose, when what is indicated by evidence is strong. The truth is that he is from the affiliated mujtahids who affiliate to a specific imam among the mujtahids, but they do not follow him blindly neither in branches nor in principles, because they are characterized by ijtihad. They only affiliated to him because they follow his method in ijtihad. And if one is lower than that, he is from the mujtahids within the school, able to extract rulings from the principles laid down by the imam. His rank never falls below this rank despite anyone who puts him down. How excellent is the statement of Mawla Abd al-Aziz al-Muhaddith al-Dihlawi in 'Bustan al-Muhaddithin' where he said something whose translation is: 'Mukhtasar al-Tahawi indicates that he was a mujtahid and not a mere blind follower of the Hanafi school, for he chose in it things contrary to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa because strong evidence appeared to him.' End. In summary, he is in the layer of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, not lower than their rank on the correct opinion. And their likes. 'Umadat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya: They are not able to make ijtihad at all, but due to their comprehensive knowledge of principles and mastery of sources, they are able to detail a general statement having two aspects, and an ambiguous ruling that could mean two things, transmitted from Abu Hanifa or from one of his companions, by their consideration and opinion in the principles, and analogy on similar branches. And what occurs in 'al-Hidayah' like 'in the takhrij of al-Razi' is of this type.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage defines the third layer of Hanafi jurists, known as 'ashab al-takhrij'. They are muqallids who nevertheless possess the ability to engage in ijtihad for cases where no explicit narration from the founding imams exists. However, they cannot contradict the school's established principles or subsidiary rulings. The text then discusses the case of al-Razi (Ahmad ibn Ali al-Jassas), noting that although he is classified here, he actually reached a higher rank of affiliated ijtihad, often differing from Abu Hanifa when strong evidence demanded it. This, the author asserts, places him in the same layer as Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage then clarifies that the true 'ashab al-takhrij' are not independent mujtahids; they cannot generate new rulings from scratch. Instead, they can resolve ambiguities in transmitted statements by applying school principles and analogical reasoning to similar cases. The example from 'al-Hidayah' referencing 'takhrij al-Razi' illustrates this category.

Key Terms
التخريج (al-takhrij): Deriving rulings from established principles (usul) for cases where no explicit text exists, by means of analogy and reasoning within the school.
المقلدون (al-muqallidun): Followers who accept the rulings of a mujtahid without requiring proof. Here, they have limitations but can still exercise some ijtihad within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary ability of ashab al-takhrij?
A) To independently create new principles (usul).
B) To issue fatwas contrary to the madhhab when evidence is strong.
C) To detail ambiguous rulings transmitted from the founders using school principles and analogy.
D) To reject all narrations in favor of their own opinion.

Key Takeaway
Ashab al-takhrij are muqallids with the capacity to derive rulings for unstated cases through analogy, without violating the school's core principles.

Introduction and Front Matter

Reclassifying al-Razi: From Muqallid to Affiliated Mujtahid
Dispute over al-Razi's classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the arguments for considering al-Razi an affiliated mujtahid rather than a mere muqallid.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's frequent disagreements with Abu Hanifa show he possessed ijtihad, elevating him above the ashab al-takhrij.

Though commonly listed among ashab al-takhrij, al-Razi (Ahmad ibn Ali al-Jassas) is argued by some to have reached a higher rank. This lesson examines the evidence from his works and the author's conclusion that he is an affiliated mujtahid.

Guided Path
1
State the classification question
The issue is whether al-Razi belongs to the third layer (ashab al-takhrij) or is a mujtahid.
2
Present evidence for muqallid view
Some argue he is a muqallid because he is often listed with them and did not claim independent ijtihad.
This is the surface classification.
3
Present evidence for mujtahid view
From his work 'Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar', he often chose opinions contrary to Abu Hanifa when strong evidence supported the opposite.
This demonstrates independent reasoning.
4
Analyze the author's argument
The author asserts that al-Razi followed Abu Hanifa's methodology but not his conclusions; this makes him an affiliated mujtahid.
Affiliated mujtahids follow the method, not the specific rulings.
5
Note the practical consequence
If al-Razi is a mujtahid, his opinions carry weight even when they oppose the well-known Hanafi position, and they can be used as evidence in dispute.
This impacts the school's fatwa hierarchy.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Fourth Layer: Ashab al-Tarjih
Defines the fourth layer of Hanafi jurists who prefer certain narrations over others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of ashab al-tarjih in the Hanafi madhhab and list the five criteria they use to prefer one narration over another.

Core Idea
Ashab al-tarjih select the strongest narration without independent ijtihad.

In the Hanafi school, not all jurists are equal. The fourth layer — ashab al-tarjih — are muqallids who weigh conflicting narrations. Their preferences shape the relied-upon positions (mufta bihi). This lesson defines their role and the criteria they apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the layer and its place
Understand that the fourth layer consists of muqallid jurists who specialize in tarjih (preference) among existing narrations. They are not independent mujtahids.
The passage calls them 'min al-muqallidin' (from the followers).
2
List the examples given
The passage explicitly names Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri and Shaykh al-Islam al-Marghinani as key ashab al-tarjih.
Al-Quduri authored Mukhtasar al-Quduri; al-Marghinani authored al-Hidayah.
3
Extract the five criteria
Memorize the five phrases: this is more appropriate (أولى), more reliable in transmission (أصح رواية), clearer in understanding (أوضح دراية), more consistent with analogy (أوفق للقياس), more beneficial for people (أرفق بالناس).
These are the tools they use to weigh narrations.
4
Differentiate from higher layers
Ashab al-tarjih do not derive new rulings; they select among transmitted opinions. This distinguishes them from mujtahids and ashab al-takhrij.
Their work is critical for determining the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة : طبقة أصحاب الترجيح من المقلدين ؛ كأبي الحسين أحمد القُدُوري، وشيخ الإسلام برهان الدين عليّ المَرْغِينَانِي صاحب الهداية»، وأمثالهما، وشأنهم تفضيل بعض الروايات على بعض آخر ، بقولهم : هذا أولى، وهذا أصح رواية، وهذا أوضح دراية، وهذا أوفق للقياس، وهذا أرفق بالناس.
The fourth: the layer of people of tarjih among the muqallids, like Abu al-Husayn Ahmad al-Quduri, and Shaykh al-Islam Burhan al-Din Ali al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, and their likes. Their concern is preferring some narrations over others by saying: this is more appropriate, this is more reliable in transmission, this is clearer in understanding, this is more consistent with analogy, this is more beneficial for people.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth layer of Hanafi jurists: ashab al-tarjih. These jurists are muqallids (followers of the school) but they are able to weigh conflicting narrations and decide which one is stronger. The text gives examples: al-Quduri (author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri) and al-Marghinani (author of al-Hidayah). They use specific criteria: preference based on suitability, reliability of narration, clarity of understanding (diraayah), conformity to analogy (qiyas), and benefit for the people. This layer is important because many of the relied-upon positions (mufta bihi) are determined by such tarjih.

Key Terms
أصحاب الترجيح (ashab al-tarjih): Jurists who prefer some narrations over others using specific criteria, without engaging in independent ijtihad.
مقلد (muqallid): A follower of a madhhab who does not perform independent ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a criterion used by ashab al-tarjih?
A) Agreement with the majority of companions.
B) More reliable in transmission.
C) Consistency with the opinion of the caliph.
D) Preference for the easier option.

Key Takeaway
Ashab al-tarjih are muqallids who select the strongest narration using criteria like reliability, clarity, analogy, and benefit.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Fifth Layer: Muqallids Who Distinguish Narrations
Defines the fifth layer of Hanafi muqallids and their distinguishing capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the capability of the fifth layer of Hanafi muqallids and state how they differ from higher layers.

Core Idea
Muqallids of the fifth layer distinguish between stronger and weaker narrations but cannot perform tarjih or ijtihad.

In the Hanafi school, jurists are classified by their level of legal reasoning. The fifth layer of muqallids are those who, while not qualified for ijtihad, have enough training to differentiate between the various strengths of narrations within the school. This lesson unpacks their specific role and place in the hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Locate the layer in the hierarchy
The fifth layer is the lowest among muqallids, meaning they do not perform tarjih but can still weigh narrations.
Higher layers can perform tarjih and ijtihad.
2
Understand what they can do
They distinguish between stronger (aqwa) and strong (qawi), weak (da'if), apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab), apparent narrations (zahir al-riwayat), and rare narrations (nawadir).
These categories are hierarchical in authority.
3
Know what they cannot do
They cannot perform independent reasoning or preference (tarjih) beyond identifying narrations.
Tarjih involves applying principles like qiyas.
4
Memorize key examples
Examples include Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari, Jamal al-Din Sayri, and Hafiz al-Din al-Kardari.
These scholars compiled fatwa collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة : طبقة المقلّدين القادرين على التمييز بين الأقوى والقوي، والضعيف وظاهر المذهب، وظاهر الروايات والروايات النادرة، كشمس الأئمة محمد الكردري ، وجمال الدين صيري، وحافظ الدين محمد الكردري ...
The fifth: the layer of muqallids who are able to distinguish between the stronger and the strong, the weak and the apparent (zahir) of the madhhab, and the apparent narrations and the rare narrations, such as Shams al-A'immah Muhammad al-Kardari, Jamal al-Din Sayri, and Hafiz al-Din Muhammad al-Kardari ...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage describes the fifth and lowest layer of Hanafi jurists among the muqallids. These jurists cannot perform ijtihad or even tarjih on their own, but they have enough knowledge of the school's principles to distinguish between different levels of narrations: the stronger vs. strong, weak, the apparent position of the school (zahir al-madhhab), and the difference between widely transmitted narrations (zahir al-riwayah) and rare ones (nawadir). They can thus apply the correct ruling without engaging in independent reasoning. The examples given include Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari and others, indicating that this layer includes many later jurists who compiled fatwa collections.

Key Terms
ظاهر الروايات (zahir al-riwayat): The narrations that are widely transmitted and considered the authoritative position of the school (equivalent to zahir al-riwayah).
الروايات النادرة (al-riwayat al-nadirah): Rare narrations that are not part of the widely transmitted corpus; they are less authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary function of the fifth layer jurists according to the passage?
A) To perform independent ijtihad on new issues.
B) To prefer one narration over another using criteria like qiyas.
C) To distinguish between different strengths of narrations and the apparent school position.
D) To create new principles of jurisprudence.

Key Takeaway
The fifth-layer muqallid can distinguish between different strengths of narrations in the Hanafi school, ensuring that the strongest narrations are followed.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Strata of Hanafi Jurists: From Mujtahids to Muqallids
Classification of Hanafi jurists into five strata with their roles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Hanafi jurists into five strata and identify the authority of their works.

Core Idea
Hanafi legal authority is tiered: mujtahids, then jurists who prefer narrations (ashab al-tarjih), then those who select sound narrations (mutun authors), and finally laymen bound to follow.

Not all Hanafi scholars possess the same authority. The madhhab developed a clear hierarchy from the founding mujtahids down to lay muqallids. This lesson examines two critical middle strata: those who can prefer one narration over another (ashab al-tarjih) and those who can distinguish strong from weak narrations to produce reliable texts (the fifth stratum). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for knowing which works and opinions carry the greatest weight in fatwa and practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Five Strata
Review the overall Hanafi classification of jurists: mujtahidun fi al-shar', mujtahidun fi al-madhhab, ashab al-takhrij, ashab al-tarjih, and muqallids capable of distinguishing (plus general muqallids). This lesson focuses on the fourth and fifth.
The source passage begins with the fourth stratum.
2
Analyze the Fourth Stratum: Ashab al-Tarjih
Examine the role of ashab al-tarjih (e.g., al-Quduri, al-Marghinani). They prefer one narration over another using criteria like authenticity, clarity, conformity to qiyas, and benefit to people. They do not derive new rulings but weigh existing transmissions.
Their statements like 'this is more appropriate' are not ijtihad but tarjih.
3
Analyze the Fifth Stratum: Muqallids Capable of Distinguishing
These jurists (e.g., al-Kardari, al-Nasafi, authors of al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqaya, al-Majma') can distinguish between strong and weak positions, and between zahir al-riwaya and nawadir. They produce concise texts that exclude weak opinions.
This is considered the lowest class of jurists (adna tabaqat al-mutafaqqihin).
4
Understand the Role of Laymen
Below the fifth stratum are general muqallids who cannot distinguish strong from weak. They must simply narrate fatwas from reliable scholars and cannot issue independent fatwas.
The passage stresses that such laymen may only give fatwa by way of hikayah (narration).
5
Consider Disputes and Nuances in Classification
The footnotes show disagreements: some scholars like Ibn al-Humam and al-Nasafi are placed by some in higher strata (mujtahid fi al-madhhab). Recognize that classifications can be contested but the general framework is widely accepted.
This reflects the non-dogmatic nature of the Hanafi hierarchy.

الرابعة : طبقة أصحاب الترجيح من المقلدين ؛ كأبي الحسين أحمد القُدُوري، وشيخ الإسلام برهان الدين عليّ المَرْغِينَانِي صاحب الهداية»، وأمثالهما، وشأنهم تفضيل بعض الروايات على بعض آخر ، بقولهم : هذا أولى، وهذا أصح رواية، وهذا أوضح دراية، وهذا أوفق للقياس، وهذا أرفق بالناس. والخامسة : طبقة المقلّدين القادرين على التمييز بين الأقوى والقوي، والضعيف وظاهر المذهب، وظاهر الروايات والروايات النادرة، كشمس الأئمة محمد الكردري ، وجمال الدين صيري )، وحافظ الدين النَّسَفِي)، وغيرهم مثل أصحاب المتون من المتأخّر كصاحب «المختار" وصاحب «الوقاية»، وصاحب «المجمع»(۳). وشأنهم أن لا ينقلوا في كتبهم الأقوال المردودة، والروايات الضعيفة، وهذه الطبقة أدنى طبقات المتفقهين. وأما الذين هم دون ذلك فإنّهم كانوا ناقصين عامين يلزمهم تقليد علماء عصرهم وفقهاء دهرهم، ولا يحل لهم أن يفتوا إلا بطريق الحكاية، فيحكي ما يضبطه من أفواه العلماء، ويحفظه من أقوال الفقهاء . انتهى كلامه

(۱) قال الإمام اللكنوي في «النافع الكبير» (ص۱۲ - ۱۳) : ومن أصحاب التخريج الفقيه أبو عبد الله الجرجاني، ويدلّ عليه كلام صاحب «الهداية» في باب صفة الصلاة، ثم القومة والجلسة سنة عندهما، وكذا الطمأنينة في تخريج الجرجاني. وفي تخريج : واجبة، حتى تجب سجدتا السهو بتركها عنده.

(۳) سيأتي ردَّ هذا بعد قليل.

(٥) هو محمد بن عبد الستار، تلميذ صاحب ((الهداية) المتوفى سنة (٦٤٢) وكردر كجعفر قرية منه رحمه الله . أقول : انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية في زمانه. ينظر: «الجواهر»(۳: ۲۲۸ «تاج»(ص٢٦٧ - ٨ - ٢٦٨). (النجوم الزاهرة (٦ : ٣٥١).

تلميذ حسن بن منصور قاضي خان كانت وفاته سنة (٦٣٦) منه رحمه الله. أقول : قال الإمام اللكنوي في «النافع الكبير» (ص ٥٦) : «كان إماماً فاضلاً انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية، ومن تصانیفه شرحان للجامع الكبير : أحدهما مختصر والآخر مطول سماه «التحرير» و«شرح السير الكبير»، وقدم الشام، ودرس، وأفتى».
(۱) وهو عبد الله أحمد بن بن محمود النسفي ، أبو البركات، حافظ الدين ، قال الإمام اللكنوي : وكل تصانيفه نافعةٌ مُعتبرة عند الفقهاء مطروحة لأنظار العلماء. من مؤلفاته : «الكافي شرح الوافي»، و«الكنز»، و«تفسير المدارك)، (ت ۷۰۱ هـ) . ينظر : «الجواهر المضية (٢ : ٢٩٤)، و «الفوائد» (ص۱۰۲)، و«تاج»(ص١٧٤).
قال اللكنوي في «التعليقات السنية»(ص ١٠١ – ١٠٢): «النسفي... عده ابن كمال باشا من طبقة المقلدين القادرين على التمييز بين القوي والضعيف، الذين شَأنهم أن لا ينقلوا في كتبهم الأقوال المردودة ، والروايات الضعيفة، وهي أدنى طبقات المتفقهين، منحطة عن درجة المجتهدين والمخرجين. وعده غيره من المجتهدين في المذهب ، قال : إنه اختتم به، ولم يُوجد بعده مجتهد في المذهب».
(۲) وهو عبد الله بن محمود بن مَوْدُود الموصلي الحنفي، أبو الفضل، مجد الدين، قال الكفوي : وكان من أفراد الدهر في الفروع والأصول، وكانت مشاهير الفتاوى على حفظه. من مؤلفاته : «المختار» وشرحه «الاختيار لتعليل المختار للفتوى والمشتمل على مسائل المختصر، (٥٩٩ - ٦٨٣ هـ) . ينظر : «الجواهر (۲) : ٣٤٩ - ٣٥٠)، وتاج التراجم ( ص ١٧٦ . ۱۷۷)، و«الفوائد»(ص۱۸۰).
(۳) وهو أحمد بن علي بن ثعلب السَّاعَاتِي البعلبكي البغدادي ، مظفر الدين، وأبوه هو الذي عمل الساعات المشهورة ببغداد ، قال :الكفوي كان إمام العصر في العلوم الشرعية، كان ثقة حافظا متقناً ، أقر له شيوخ زمانه بأنه فارس جواد في ميدانه. من مؤلفاته «مجمع البحرين»، و«بديع النظام»، (ت٦٩٤هـ). ينظر : «النافع الكبير» (ص ۲۵)، و«مرآة الجنان»(٤ : ٢٢٧)، والكشف» (٢ : ١٦٠٠).
The fourth: the class of those who give preference (tarjih) among the muqallids, such as Abu al-Husayn Ahmad al-Quduri, Shaykh al-Islam Burhan al-Din Ali al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, and their likes. Their role is to prefer some narrations over others, saying: this is more appropriate, this is more sound in narration, this is clearer in understanding, this is more in accordance with analogy, this is more beneficial for people. The fifth: the class of muqallids who are capable of distinguishing between the stronger and the strong, the weak, the apparent [position] of the madhhab, the apparent narrations and the rare narrations, such as Shams al-Aimmah Muhammad al-Kardari, Jamal al-Din al-Sairi, Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi, and others like the authors of legal texts (mutun) among the later scholars, such as the author of al-Mukhtar, the author of al-Wiqaya, and the author of al-Majma'. Their role is that they do not transmit rejected opinions and weak narrations in their books. This class is the lowest class of the jurists. As for those below that, they are deficient laymen, obligated to follow the scholars of their time and the jurists of their era. It is not permissible for them to give fatwas except by way of narration; so he narrates what he records from the mouths of scholars and preserves from the statements of jurists. End of his words.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a classification of Hanafi jurists into strata, as presented by the commentator of al-Wiqaya. It describes the fourth and fifth strata as well as those below them. The fourth stratum (طبقة أصحاب الترجيح) consists of muqallids who are capable of tarjih (preferring one narration over another) based on criteria such as authenticity, clarity, conformity to qiyas, and public benefit. Prominent examples are al-Quduri and al-Marghinani. The fifth stratum (طبقة المقلدين القادرين على التمييز) comprises muqallids who can distinguish between strong and weak positions and know the zahir al-riwaya from the nawadir. They produce concise texts (mutun) that exclude weak and rejected opinions. Below them are the 'awamm (laymen) who cannot give fatwas independently and must simply narrate the fatwa of their teachers. The commentator then provides extensive footnotes (in parentheses) naming figures from different strata and citing authorities like al-Lakhnawi and al-Kafawi, offering biographical details and clarifying the status of certain scholars like Ibn al-Humam and al-Nasafi. The passage thus serves as a guide to the Hanafi scholarly hierarchy, essential for understanding the authority of various works and the weight of opinions.

Key Terms
أصحاب الترجيح (ashab al-tarjih): The class of muqallid jurists who have the ability to prefer one narration or opinion over another within the Hanafi school, using criteria such as authenticity, conformity to analogy, and benefit to people.
المقلدين القادرين على التمييز (al-muqallidin al-qadirina 'ala al-tamyiz): Muqallids who can distinguish between strong and weak positions, and between zahir al-riwaya and nawadir. They produce reliable mutun that exclude weak opinions.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known and transmitted opinions from the founding imams, as recorded in the six major books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which stratum do authors of standard Hanafi texts like al-Mukhtar and al-Wiqaya belong to?
A) The fourth stratum (ashab al-tarjih)
B) The fifth stratum (muqallids capable of distinguishing)
C) The third stratum (ashab al-takhrij)
D) The first stratum (mujtahidun fi al-shar')

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies its jurists into distinct strata; reliance on a fatwa depends on the stratum of the scholar issuing it, with the highest authority from the founding mujtahids, then the authors of standard texts, and finally the 'awamm who can only narrate.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Seven Layers of Hanafi Jurists: Classification and Correction
Critique and refinement of jurist hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the seven layers of Hanafi jurists and identify the error in al-Durr al-Mukhtar regarding the extinction of absolute mujtahids.

Core Idea
The Hanafi hierarchy distinguishes absolute mujtahids, restricted mujtahids, and muqallids — but classifications must correctly place each scholar.

In this passage, 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi critiques the popular seven-layer classification of Hanafi jurists. He clarifies that the absolute mujtahid (like the four Imams) belongs to the first layer, not extinct as claimed by some. He also corrects the notion that restricted mujtahids have seven ranks — they have five. This lesson unpacks the classification and the refinement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven layers
From the text, note the first layer (absolute mujtahids) and the seventh layer (muqallids). The intermediate layers are implied but not detailed in this passage.
The full seven layers are often: 1. absolute mujtahid, 2. restricted mujtahid, 3. tarjih, 4. tamyiz, 5. talfiq, 6. ashab al-wujuh, 7. muqallid.
2
Understand the fivefold vs sevenfold distinction
The fivefold classification excludes both the first and seventh layers (absolute mujtahids and blind muqallids). The sevenfold includes them. Both are valid depending on purpose.
Al-Lakhnawi says there is no contradiction, as they cover different ranges.
3
Analyze the correction of al-Durr al-Mukhtar
The author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar claimed that absolute mujtahids are extinct and restricted mujtahids are on seven ranks. Al-Lakhnawi says absolute mujtahids are still part of the seven ranks, and the seventh rank is not ijtihad; thus restricted mujtahids should be on five ranks.
This correction ensures the classification remains comprehensive.
4
Recognize the incomplete critique
The passage ends mid-sentence, hinting at further objections, such as the placement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Be aware that this is an ongoing refinement.
Later passages (not provided) would complete the critique.

وذكر عمر بن عمر الأزهري (1) المصري في آخر كتاب «الجواهر النفيسة شرح الدرة المنيفة في مذهب أبي حنيفة» ، وعلى القاري (2) المكي في رسالته في «ذمّ الروافض»، وغيرهما من محشي «الدر المختار»(3) وغيرهم ، نقلاً عن ابن كمال باشا، مؤلف الإصلاح والإيضاح، وسيأتي إن شاء الله ذكره : إن الفقهاء على سبع طبقات، فذكر خمس طبقات نحو ما مر ذكره، وزاد : الطبقة الأولى : وهي طبقة المجتهدين بالاجتهاد المطلق، كالأئمة الأربعة، ومن سلك مسلكهم في تأسيس قواعد الأصول، واستنباط أحكام الفروع عن الأدلة الأربعة من غير تقليد لأحدٍ لا في الفروع ولا في الأصول. والطبقة السابعة : وهي طبقة المقلّدين الذين لا يقدرون على ما ذكر، ولا يفرقون بين الغث والسمين، ولا يميزون بين الشمال واليمين، بل يحفظون ما يجدون، كحاطب ليل، فالويل لهم ولمن قلّدهم كلّ الويل (انتهى)
ثم قال: قلت) : لا منافاة بين التخميس والتسبيع، فإنّ مَن خَمْسَ اقتصر على الفقهاء الذين لم يبلغوا درجة الاجتهاد المطلق، ولم يخطوا عن درجة التمييز بين الضعيف والقوي، ولم يصلوا إلى درجة التقليد المطلق، ومَن سبع عمَّم فأدخل في القسمة المجتهدين المطلقين، والعلماء الغير المميزين. وقد زل قدم صاحب «الدر المختار شرح تنوير الأبصار» حيث قال : «قد ذكروا أنَّ المجتهد المطلق قد فقد ، وأما المقيّد فعلى سبع مراتب مشهورة». انتهى فإن المجتهد المطلق داخل في المراتب السبع لا خارج عنها، والمرتبة السابعة ليست من مراتب الاجتهاد لا المطلق والمقيد، فالصواب أن يقول : وأما المقيّد فعلى خمس مراتب مشهورة. وليعلم أن هذه القسمة مسبعة كانت أو مخمسة وإن كانت صحيحة، لكن في اندراج الفقهاء المذكورين الذين أدرجهم أصحاب التقسيمات بحسب زعمهم في قسم قسم تحت ذلك القسم نظراً من وجوه : ١. منها : أنهم أدرجوا أبا يوسف ومحمد الله في طبقة مجتهدي المذهب، الذين لا
And [he] mentioned 'Umar ibn 'Umar al-Azhari (1) the Egyptian at the end of the book 'al-Jawahir al-Nafisah Sharh al-Durrah al-Munifah fi Madhhab Abi Hanifah', and [he mentioned] 'Ali al-Qari (2) al-Makki in his treatise on 'Dhamm al-Rawafid', and others from the commentators of 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' (3) and others, quoting from Ibn Kamal Pasha, author of 'al-Islah wal-Idah', and it will come, God willing, his mention: that the jurists are on seven layers. So he mentioned five layers similar to what was previously mentioned, and added: The first layer: it is the layer of absolute mujtahids, like the four Imams and those who followed their path in establishing the principles of usul and deriving the rulings of branches from the four proofs without taqlid of anyone, neither in branches nor in principles. And the seventh layer: it is the layer of muqallids who are not able to what was mentioned, and they do not distinguish between the bad and the good, nor do they differentiate between the north and the south, but they memorize what they find, like one who gathers firewood at night, so woe to them and woe to those who imitate them (end). Then he said: I say: there is no contradiction between the fivefold and sevenfold [division]. For the one who made it five restricted himself to the jurists who did not reach the degree of absolute ijtihad, nor step beyond the degree of distinguishing between weak and strong, nor reach the degree of absolute taqlid, and the one who made it seven generalized and included in the division the absolute mujtahids and the non-distinguishing scholars. And the foot of the author of 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar Sharh Tanwir al-Absar' slipped where he said: 'They mentioned that the absolute mujtahid has become extinct, and as for the restricted [mujtahid], he is on seven well-known ranks.' End. For the absolute mujtahid is included in the seven ranks, not outside them, and the seventh rank is not from the ranks of ijtihad, neither absolute nor restricted. So the correct [statement] is to say: 'As for the restricted [mujtahid], he is on five well-known ranks.' And let it be known that this division, whether sevenfold or fivefold, even if correct, yet the inclusion of the mentioned jurists whom the authors of the divisions included, according to their claim, in each division under that division is open to consideration from several aspects: 1. Among them: that they included Abu Yusuf and Muhammad [al-Shaybani] in the layer of mujtahids of the madhhab, who are not...
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the classification of Hanafi jurists into seven layers, as attributed to Ibn Kamal Pasha. The author, 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, begins by citing earlier scholars who reported this classification: 'Umar al-Azhari, 'Ali al-Qari, and others. The first layer consists of absolute mujtahids like the four Imams who derived rulings independently from the four proofs without taqlid. The seventh layer is of blind muqallids who cannot distinguish between sound and weak rulings and merely memorize what they find. Al-Lakhnawi then notes that there is no contradiction between a fivefold and sevenfold division: the fivefold division excludes absolute mujtahids and non-distinguishing scholars, while the sevenfold division includes them. He corrects the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar who claimed that absolute mujtahid is extinct, explaining that the absolute mujtahid is part of the seven ranks. The correct statement is that the restricted mujtahid is on five ranks. Finally, al-Lakhnawi raises objections to the classifications, the first being that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani were placed in the layer of mujtahids of the madhhab, which seems problematic. The passage ends abruptly, but it sets the stage for further critique of how specific scholars are categorized.

Key Terms
طبقة (tabaqa): A rank or layer of jurists according to their level of ijtihad and taqlid.
مجتهد مطلق (mujtahid mutlaq): A jurist who can derive rulings from the primary sources independently without following any madhhab.
مجتهد مقيّد (mujtahid muqayyad): A jurist who derives rulings within the confines of a specific madhhab, using its principles.
مقلّد (muqallid): A layperson or scholar who follows a mujtahid without knowing the evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Lakhnawi's correction, how many layers of restricted mujtahids (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad) are there?
A) Seven
B) Five
C) Six
D) One

Key Takeaway
Absolute mujtahids form the first layer of Hanafi jurists, and restricted mujtahids have five layers — the seventh layer is muqallids, not ijtihad.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Three Mutūn and Their Authority in the Hanafi School
Explains the levels of matn and identifies key Hanafi texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three most authoritative mutūn in the Hanafi school and explain the general but not absolute rule regarding their transmission of Zāhir al-Riwāyah.

Core Idea
The mutūn are relied upon for Zāhir al-Riwāyah, but authors sometimes include derived opinions that contradict the original madhhab.

In the Hanafi school, not every text carries the same weight. Scholars have identified a set of abridgments (mutūn) that form the backbone of the madhhab. This lesson unpacks which texts are considered the most authoritative, what they typically transmit, and when they might deviate from the core doctrine. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for navigating Hanafi fiqh literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of 'mutūn'
Begin by noting that 'mutūn' in the Hanafi context refers to specific abridgments authored by senior jurists, not any summary. These texts are given precedence in fatwa.
Authors like al-Ṭaḥāwī, al-Karkhī, al-Ḥākim al-Shahīd, and al-Qudūrī are from the first layer.
2
List the key texts and their authors
Memorize the six texts mentioned: al-Wiqāyah, Kanz al-Daqā’iq, al-Mukhtār, Majma‘ al-Baḥrayn, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī. Note that the first three are the most relied upon.
Dates help identify the era: al-Qudūrī died in 428 AH, al-Mawṣilī in 683 AH, al-Nasafī in 710 AH.
3
Understand the 'three mutūn' and 'four mutūn'
When scholars say 'the three mutūn', they mean al-Wiqāyah, al-Kanz, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī. 'The four mutūn' adds either al-Mukhtār or Majma‘ al-Baḥrayn.
This terminology is used in fatwa literature.
4
Recognize exceptions to the rule
The mutūn generally transmit Zāhir al-Riwāyah and the madhhab of Abū Ḥanīfah, but this is not absolute. They sometimes include takhrījāt of earlier mashāyikh that contradict the original madhhab, e.g., the 'one-tenth upon one-tenth' rule. They also occasionally prefer the ṣāḥibayn's views, as in prostration with forehead and nose.
Be aware that the mutūn are authoritative but not infallible.

Source Text

الدراسة الثالثة: طبقات المسائل
لأنَّ المراد بالمذهب ما يذكرُ في كتب ظاهر الرواية وهاهنا كل من القولين صرحوا بأنه ظاهر الرواية، فحيث كان كذلك فعلينا اتباع ما صرحوا لنا بتصحيحه». انتهى ثم المراد بالمتون في قولهم : ما في المتون مقدم، ليس جميع المتون ، بل المختصرات التي ألفها حداق الأئمة، وكبار الفقهاء المعروفين بالعلم والزهد والفقه والثقة في الرواية، كأبي جعفر الطحاوي والكَرْخي والحاكم الشهيد والقُدُوري، ومن في هذه الطبقة (1).
وقد كثر اعتماد المتأخرين على «الوقاية لبرهان الشريعة، و«كنز الدقائق» لأبي البركات حافظ الدين عبد الله بن أحمد النَّسَفِي ، المتوفى سنة عشرة وسبعمئة ، و«المختار» لأبي الفضل مجد الدين عبد الله بن محمود الموصلي، المتوفى سنة ثلاث وثمانين وستمئة ، ومجمع «البحرين» المظفر الدين أحمد بن علي البغدادي المتوفى سنة أربع وتسعين وستمئة، و«مختصر القدوري لأحمد بن محمد المتوفى سنة ثمان وعشرين وأربعمئة ؛ وذلك لما علموا من جلالة مؤلّفيها ، والتزامهم إيراد مسائل معتمد عليها (2). وأشهرها ذكراً، وأقواها اعتماداً: «الوقاية»، و«الكنز»، و«مختصر القدوري»، وهي المراد بقولهم : المتون الثلاثة، وإذا أطلقوا المتون الأربعة أرادوا هذه الثلاثة : و«المختار»، أو «المجمع».
واعلم أنه قد اشتهر أنَّ المتون موضوعةٌ لنقل أصل المذهب ومسائل ظاهر الرواية، وهذا حكم غالبيّ لا كلي، فإنّه كثيراً ما يذكر أرباب المتون مسألة هي من تخريجات المشايخ المتقدمين، مخالفة لمسلكِ الأئمة المتبوعين : كمسألة (العشر في العشر في باب نجاسة الحوض وطهارته)، فإنّها من تحديدات المشايخ المتقدمين، وأصل المذهب خال عن هذا ، كما ستعرفه في موضعِهِ إن شاء الله تعالى.
وكذا ما اشتهر أنّ المتون موضوعةٌ لنقل مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة، حكم غالبي لا أكثري ، فكثيراً ما ذكروا فيها مذهب صاحبيه إذا كان راجحاً، كما في بحث (السجدة بالجبهة والأنف) وغيره.
Third study: Layers of the masā’il (legal issues). Because what is meant by 'madhhab' is what is mentioned in the books of Zāhir al-Riwāyah, and here each of the two statements explicitly states that it is Zāhir al-Riwāyah. So when it is like that, it is obligatory upon us to follow what they have clarified for us as correct. End. Then what is meant by 'al-mutūn' in their statement 'what is in the mutūn is given precedence' is not all mutūn, but rather the abridgments authored by the sharpest of the imams and the senior jurists known for knowledge, asceticism, jurisprudence, and reliability in transmission, such as Abū Ja‘far al-Ṭaḥāwī, al-Karkhī, al-Ḥākim al-Shahīd, al-Qudūrī, and those of this level. The later scholars have greatly relied on 'al-Wiqāyah' by Burhān al-Sharī‘ah, 'Kanz al-Daqā’iq' by Abū al-Barakāt Ḥāfiẓ al-Dīn ‘Abdullāh ibn Aḥmad al-Nasafī (d. 710 AH), 'al-Mukhtār' by Abū al-Faḍl Majd al-Dīn ‘Abdullāh ibn Maḥmūd al-Mawṣilī (d. 683 AH), 'Majma‘ al-Baḥrayn' by al-Muẓaffar al-Dīn Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī al-Baghdādī (d. 694 AH), and 'Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī' by Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad (d. 428 AH). This is due to what they knew of the eminence of their authors and their commitment to presenting relied-upon issues. The most renowned in mention and the strongest in reliability are 'al-Wiqāyah', 'al-Kanz', and 'Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī'; they are what is meant by their statement 'the three mutūn'. When they use 'the four mutūn', they intend these three plus 'al-Mukhtār' or 'al-Majma‘'. Know that it is well known that the mutūn are intended to transmit the original madhhab and the issues of Zāhir al-Riwāyah. This is a predominant ruling, not universal; for indeed, many a time the authors of the mutūn mention an issue which is from the derivations (takhrijāt) of the earlier mashāyikh, contradicting the way of the followed imams—like the issue of 'one-tenth upon one-tenth' in the chapter on the impurity and purity of the basin; for it is from the determinations of the early mashāyikh, and the original madhhab is devoid of this, as you will learn in its place, God willing. Likewise, what is well known that the mutūn are intended to transmit the madhhab of Imam Abū Ḥanīfah is a predominant ruling, not a majority ruling; for indeed, they frequently mention in them the madhhab of his two companions if it is preponderant, as in the discussion of 'prostration with the forehead and nose' and others.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion on the layers of legal texts (mutūn) in the Hanafi school. It first clarifies that when scholars say 'what is in the mutūn is given precedence', they refer to specific abridgments authored by elite early jurists like al-Ṭaḥāwī, al-Karkhī, al-Ḥākim al-Shahīd, and al-Qudūrī. Later scholars heavily relied on four key texts: al-Wiqāyah (by Burhān al-Sharī‘ah), Kanz al-Daqā’iq (by al-Nasafī), al-Mukhtār (by al-Mawṣilī), and Majma‘ al-Baḥrayn (by al-Baghdādī), but the most famous trio is al-Wiqāyah, al-Kanz, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī. When 'the four mutūn' is mentioned, it means these three plus either al-Mukhtār or al-Majma‘. The passage then corrects a common misconception: the mutūn predominantly transmit Zāhir al-Riwāyah (the core transmitted positions from Imām Muḥammad's six books) and the madhhab of Imām Abū Ḥanīfah, but this is not absolute. Authors sometimes include issues derived by later mashāyikh that contradict the original madhhab, like the 'one-tenth upon one-tenth' rule for basin purity. They also occasionally mention the positions of Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad (the ṣāḥibayn) when those are preponderant, as in the prostration using forehead and nose. Thus, the mutūn are authoritative but not infallible guides; one must be aware of the occasional exceptions.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutūn): In this context, the specific abridgments of fiqh authored by senior Hanafi jurists that are relied upon for transmitting the madhhab.
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The manifest narrations from Imām Muḥammad al-Shaybānī's six core books, forming the primary authority of the Hanafi madhhab.
المتون الثلاثة (al-mutūn al-thalāthah): The three most relied-upon matn: al-Wiqāyah, Kanz al-Daqā’iq, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which three texts are referred to as 'al-mutūn al-thalāthah' (the three matn) in the Hanafi school?
A) al-Wiqāyah, al-Mukhtār, and Majma‘ al-Baḥrayn
B) Kanz al-Daqā’iq, al-Mukhtār, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī
C) al-Wiqāyah, Kanz al-Daqā’iq, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī
D) al-Wiqāyah, Majma‘ al-Baḥrayn, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī

Key Takeaway
The three chief mutūn are al-Wiqāyah, Kanz al-Daqā’iq, and Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī; they predominantly transmit the core madhhab but occasionally include exceptional derived rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Identifying Unreliable Hanafi Fiqh Works
Lists and critiques unreliable Hanafi fiqh works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify unreliable Hanafi fiqh works and explain why they are not authoritative for deriving rulings.

Core Idea
Not every book labeled 'Hanafi' is reliable; only those from trusted scholars and sound transmissions are valid for fatwa.

In the Hanafi school, not all books are created equal. While many works claim to represent the madhhab, scholars have identified certain books and authors that transmit weak or deviant opinions. This lesson examines some of these unreliable works and the criteria that disqualify them, enabling you to practice critical source evaluation.

Guided Path
1
List the works and authors
Identify each unreliable book and its author as mentioned in the passage: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya by al-Quhistani, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya by Abu al-Makarim, Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi by al-Dawlabadi, and works of al-Zahidi (al-Quniya, al-Hawi, al-Mujtaba, Zad al-A'imma), and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj by Abu Bakr ibn Ali.
Some authors like Abu al-Makarim are unknown; others like al-Zahidi are criticized for weak transmissions.
2
Understand the criticisms
Analyze the reasons each work is deemed unreliable. Abu al-Makarim is an unknown man. Al-Quhistani is described as a book dealer who mixed sound and weak material without verification, relying on al-Zahidi's Mu'tazili-influenced books. Al-Zahidi's transmissions are considered weak unless corroborated. Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi is rejected based on testimony of a later scholar.
The key critiques are: unknown author, lack of verification, reliance on weak sources, and deviation from established Hanafi rules.
3
Apply the principle of transmission
Ibn Abidin states that a muqallid must follow the madhhab of his Imam as transmitted by reliable Imams. Transmissions from al-Zahidi or al-Quhistani do not counter the established Nu'mani (Hanafi) books unless supported by other strong evidence.
The principle: only transmissions from recognized Hanafi authorities (e.g., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) carry weight when consistent with the school's usul.
4
Recognize the broader lesson
This passage teaches that source criticism is essential in fiqh. A book being 'Hanafi' in name does not guarantee its reliability. Later scholars like Ibn Abidin and Ali al-Qari provide tools to distinguish authentic works from those that may misrepresent the school.
Always cross-check evidence from primary Hanafi works (Zahir al-Riwayah) and consult established commentaries like al-Hidayah before accepting a ruling from lesser-known sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة
من الكتب الغير المعتبرة: «شرح مختصر الوقاية» للقُهستاني شمس الدين محمد مفتي بخارا، المتوفى سنة خمسين أو اثنتين وستين بعد تسعمئة المشهور بـ«جامع الرموز»، و«شرح مختصر الوقاية لأبي المكــارم.
قال ابن عابدين في «تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية» في «بحث كراهة لبس الثوب الأحمر» في أثناء الردّ على الشرنبلالي القائل بجوازه المستند إلى كلام أبي المكــارم والقهستاني: على أن الذي يجب على المقلد اتباع مذهب إمامه. والظاهر أن ما نقله هؤلاء الأئمّةُ هو مذهب الإمام لا ما نقله أبو المكــارم، فإنّه رجل مجهول، وكتابه كذلك، والقُهُسْتَانِيُّ كجارفِ سيل وحاطب ليل خُصُوصاً واستناده إلى كتب الزاهدي المعتزلي. انتهى.
وقال على القاري المكي في رسالته: «شم العوارض في ذم الروافض»: «لقد صدق عصام الدين في حق القهستاني أنه لم يكن من تلاميذ شيخ الإسلام الهروي، لا من أعاليهم، ولا من أدانيهم، وإنّما كان دلال الكتب في زمانه، ولا كان يعرف بالفقه وغيره بين أقرانه، ويؤيده أنه يجمعُ في «شرحه» هذا بين الغث والسمين، والصحيح والضعيف من غير تحقيق وتدقيق، فهو كحاطب الليل، الجامع بين الرطب واليابس في الليل». انتهى.
ومن الكتب الغير المعتبرة: «فتاوى إبراهيم شاهي» من مؤلفات القاضي شهاب الدين الدولة آبادي، كما نقله عبد القادر البدايوني في «منتخب التواريخ» عن أستاذه العلامة، أجلّ علماء العهد الأكبري الشيخ حاتم السنبهلي، المتوفى سنة ثمان وستين بعد تسعمئة.
ومنها: تصانيف نجم الدين مختار بن محمود بن محمد الزاهدي، المعتزلي الاعتقاد، حنفي الفروع، المتوفى سنة ست وخمسين وستمئة، كـ«القنية»، و«الحاوي»، و«المجتبى شرح مختصر القدوري»، و«زاد الأئمة»، وغير ذلك، فقد قال في «تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية»: «نقل الزاهدي لا يعارض نقل المعتبرات النعمانية، فإنه ذكر ابنُ وهبان: إنّه لا يلتفت إلى ما نقله صاحب «القنية» مخالفاً للقواعد، ما لم يعضده نقل من غيره، ومثله في «النهر» أيضاً. انتهى. وفيه أيضاً في موضع آخر: ««الحاوي» للزاهدي: مشهور بنقل الروايات الضعيفة». انتهى.
ومنها: «السراج الوهاج شرح مختصر القُدُوري» من مؤلفات أبي بكر بن علي.
Benefit: Among the unreliable books: 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya' by al-Quhistani Shams al-Din Muhammad, mufti of Bukhara, died 950 or 962 AH, well-known as 'Jami' al-Rumuz'; and 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya' by Abu al-Makarim. Ibn Abidin said in 'Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya' in the 'Discussion on the dislike of wearing red clothing' while refuting al-Shurunbulali who permitted it based on the words of Abu al-Makarim and al-Quhistani: 'Indeed, what is obligatory upon the muqallid is to follow the madhhab of his Imam. And it is apparent that what these Imams transmitted is the madhhab of the Imam, not what Abu al-Makarim transmitted, for he is an unknown man, and his book likewise. And al-Quhistani is like a flood and a night collector, especially since he relies on the books of al-Zahidi the Mu'tazili.' End quote. Ali al-Qari al-Makki said in his treatise 'Shamm al-'Awarid fi Dhamm al-Rawafid': 'Asim al-Din spoke the truth about al-Quhistani: he was not among the students of Shaykh al-Islam al-Harawi, neither among their elite nor among their commoners. Rather, he was a book dealer in his time, and he was not known for fiqh or other sciences among his peers. This is supported by the fact that he collected in his 'Sharh' both worthless and good, sound and weak, without verification or precision. So he is like one who gathers firewood at night, collecting wet and dry in the dark.' End quote. Among the unreliable books: 'Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi' from the works of Qadi Shihab al-Din al-Dawlabadi, as reported by 'Abd al-Qadir al-Badayuni in 'Muntakhab al-Tawarikh' from his teacher, the great scholar of the Akbari era, Shaykhat al-Sunbuhuli, died 968 AH. And among them: the works of Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad al-Zahidi, the Mu'tazili in creed, Hanafi in branches, died 656 AH, such as 'al-Quniya', 'al-Hawi', 'al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri', 'Zad al-A'imma', and others. For it was said in 'Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya': 'The transmission of al-Zahidi does not counter the transmissions of the reliable Nu'mani books. For Ibn Wahban mentioned that no attention is paid to what the author of 'al-Quniya' transmitted opposing the rules, unless supported by another transmission. Similarly in 'al-Nahr.' End quote. And in it also in another place: 'al-Hawi by al-Zahidi is well-known for transmitting weak narrations.' End quote. And among them: 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' from the works of Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of unreliable Hanafi fiqh books. The author, a commentator on al-Wiqaya, identifies several works that should not be relied upon for fatwa. First, he mentions the Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya by al-Quhistani and that by Abu al-Makarim. He quotes Ibn Abidin's critique that these authors are unknown or unreliable, and that al-Quhistani merely collected from al-Zahidi's Mu'tazili-influenced books. Then he quotes Ali al-Qari's harsh assessment, calling al-Quhistani a book dealer who mixed sound and weak material without verification. Next, he lists Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi by al-Dawlabadi, again noting its unreliability as per Badayuni's report. Then he criticizes al-Zahidi's works like al-Quniya and al-Hawi, citing Ibn Abidin that his transmissions should not oppose the established Nu'mani (Hanafi) books unless supported. Finally, he mentions al-Siraj al-Wahhaj by Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali as another unreliable commentary. The overall lesson is that one must distinguish between authoritative Hanafi works and those that contain weak or deviant opinions.

Key Terms
الغر معتبرة (ghayr mu'tabara): Books that are not considered reliable or authoritative for deriving rulings in the Hanafi school.
نقل الزاهدي (naql al-Zahidi): Transmissions from the works of Najm al-Din al-Zahidi, known for including weak or Mu'tazili-influenced narrations.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only works from recognized scholars with sound transmission chains are reliable; books like those of al-Quhistani and al-Zahidi should be avoided in fatwa.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Evaluating Trustworthy Fatwa Sources in the Hanafi School
Critical evaluation of reliable fatwa sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a Hanafi fatwa collection by applying the criteria of conformity to usul and authoritativeness of the author, and distinguish between trustworthy and weak sources.

Core Idea
A fatwa book’s authority depends on its adherence to Hanafi usul, not on its popularity.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya provides a methodological guide for muftis: not every fatwa collection can be relied upon. The author, drawing on earlier scholars like al-Birkili and Hajji Khalifa, critically examines several circulating books, highlighting the need for caution. As a student of Hanafi fiqh, understanding how to evaluate sources is essential before issuing or applying fatwas. This lesson will equip you with the criteria used by classical Hanafi authorities to separate reliable compilations from weak ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fatwa book and its source
Locate the name of the fatwa collection being discussed (e.g., 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam', 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya', 'Khulasat al-Kaydani'). Note who cited it and the chain of transmission.
The passage often gives a chain: e.g., from al-Birkili via Kashf al-Zunun.
2
Understand the assessment criterion
What does the authority say about the book? Is it called 'weak', 'unreliable', or 'widespread but unknown author'? The key criterion is conformity to the established usul (principles) of the Hanafi school.
Al-Birkili explicitly states: 'It is not from the reliable books, so it is not permissible to act by it unless it is known to agree with the principles.'
3
Apply the criterion to a specific book
For each book mentioned, determine if it meets the criterion. For example, 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya' is declared unreliable unless it agrees with usul. 'Khulasat al-Kaydani' is problematic because its author is unknown, despite its fame.
Even famous books must be scrutinized.
4
Recognize the hierarchy of authority
The passage implicitly references the hierarchy: Zahir al-Riwayah texts are most reliable; other collections are evaluated against them. The mufti must know which books are accepted by later authorities like Ibn Nujaym and al-Turi.
Later scholars like the author of Radd al-Muhtar endorse certain collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥٦ (۱) عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية الحدادي (۱) ، المتوفى سنة ثمانمئة. كما نقله صاحب «كشف الظنون»(۲) عن المولى (۳) البركلي " ومنها: «مشتمل الأحكام لفخر الدين الرومي ، كما نقلـه صــاحب الكشف»(٥) أيضاً عن البركلي. . ومنها: «الفتاوى الصوفية» لفضل الله [بن (٦) محمد بن أيوب)، تلميذ «جامع (V) المضمرات كما نقله صاحب «الكشف عن البِرْكِلي أنه قال : «إنّها ليست من الكتب المعتبرة، فلا يجوز العمل بما فيها إلا إذا علم موافقتها للأصول». (۱) وهو أبو بكر بن علي بن محمد الحَدَّادِي العبادي، أبو العتيق، رضي الدين، الشهير بصنعته ، ومن مؤلفاته : كشف التنزيل في تحقيق التأويل تفسير القرآن، وشرح منظومة شيخه العاملي» في الفقه، و «النور» المستنير شرح منظومة النسفي»، و «شرح قيد الأوابد» في الفقه وسماه «الرحيق المختوم»، و«السراج الوهاج شرح مختصر القدوري» وقد اختصره في «الجوهرة النيرة شرح مختصر القدوري»، (۷۲۰ - ۸۰۰هـ). ينظر : «تاج التراجم» (ص ١٤١)، و«الكشف (۲) : ١٦٣١). (۲) «كشف الظنون» (٢ : ١٦٣١). (۳) وهو محمد بن بير علي البركلي الرومي، محيي الدين، من مؤلفاته : «الطريقة المحمدية»، و«جلاء الأفهام»، و «متن «العوامل»، (۹۲۹ - ۹۸۱هـ). ينظر : طرب الأماثل»(ص٥٥٨) ، و«الكشف (۲ : ۱۱۱۱)، و«الحديقة الندية» (۱ : ۳). 56 (1) 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya, by al-Haddadi (1), died in the year 800. As transmitted by the author of 'Kashf al-Zunun' (2) from al-Mulla (3) al-Birkili. Among them: 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam' by Fakhr al-Din al-Rumi, as transmitted by the author of 'al-Kashf' (5) also from al-Birkili. And among them: 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya' by Fadl Allah [ibn (6) Muhammad ibn Ayyub], student of 'Jami' al-Mudmarat' (V) as transmitted by the author of 'al-Kashf' from al-Birkili that he said: 'It is not from the reliable books, so it is not permissible to act by it unless it is known to agree with the principles.' (1) He is Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Haddadi al-'Ibadi, Abu al-'Atiq, Radi al-Din, famous for his craft. Among his works: 'Kashf al-Tanzil fi Tahqiq al-Ta'wil' commentary on the Quran, 'Sharh Manzumat Shaykhihi al-'Amili' in fiqh, 'al-Nur al-Mustanir Sharh Manzumat al-Nasafi', 'Sharh Qayd al-Awabid' in fiqh which he called 'al-Rahiq al-Makhtum', 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' which he abridged into 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri', (720-800 AH). See: 'Taj al-Tarajim' (p. 141), and 'al-Kashf' (2: 1631). (2) 'Kashf al-Zunun' (2: 1631). (3) He is Muhammad ibn Bir 'Ali al-Birkili al-Rumi, Muhyi al-Din, among his works: 'al-Tariqa al-Muhammadiyya', 'Jala' al-Afham', and the text 'al-'Awamil', (929-981 AH). See: 'Tarj al-Amthal' (p. 558), and 'al-Kashf' (2: 1111), and 'al-Hadiqa al-Nadiyya' (1: 3). (4) He is Yahya al-Hanafi, Fakhr al-Din al-Rumi, among his works: 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam' in Hanafi fatwas; al-Mulla al-Birkili counted it among the weak circulating books (d. 864 AH). See: 'al-Kashf' (2: 1692). (5) 'Kashf al-Zunun' (2: 1692). (6) Not found in the original, added from 'al-Fawa'id' (p. 250). (7) He is Fadl Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Ayyub, linked to Maju; al-Kafawi said: He was a leading jurist, a principal, a master of the people of reality. Among his works: 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya'; Ibn Kamal Pasha said it is from the unreliable books. (d. 666 AH). See: 'al-Kashf' (2: 1225), and 'al-Fawa'id' (p. 250). (8) He is Yusuf ibn 'Umar ibn Yusuf al-Sufi al-Kaduri al-Bazzar al-Hanafi. Al-Kafawi said: A great elder and scholar, who combined the sciences of reality and law. Among his works: 'Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. Imam al-Laknawi said: It is a comprehensive commentary containing many branches and abundant issues (d. 832 AH). See: 'al-Kashf' (2: 1632), and 'al-Fawa'id' (p. 380). End. (1) 57 H. And among them: 'Fatawa Ibn Nujaym' and 'Fatawa al-Turi' (2), as transmitted by the author of 'Radd al-Muhtar' from 'Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud al-Azhari 'ala Sharh al-Kanz' by Mulla Miskin. 6. And among them: 'Khulasat al-Kaydani' attributed to Lutfallah al-Nasafi. Although it is famously widespread in the lands beyond the river, and they circulate it among themselves for memorization and study, yet up to now the condition of its author is not known: who he is? And how is he? And is he one whose authoritativeness is relied upon, or is he one of whom the famous proverb applies: 'Whoever does not know fiqh authored a book in it'? There is disagreement on identifying its author among three sayings reported by the author of 'Kashf al-Zunun' (4): First: That it is by Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Fanari (0), died in the year 834 AH, and he is the grandfather of Hasan Jilibi, the annotator of 'al-Mutawwal' and 'al-Talwih' and others. This was mentioned by Mulla Ahmad, known as Tashkopri Zadeh al-Rumi (6) in his commentary on the aforementioned introduction. Second: That it is by Ibn Kamal Pasha al-Rumi (8), author of 'al-Idah wa al-Islah', mentioned (1) from 'Kashf al-Zunun' (2: 1225). (2) He is Muhammad ibn Husayn ibn 'Ali al-Turi al-Qadiri al-Hanafi, among his works: 'al-Fawakih al-Turiyya fi al-Hawadith al-Misriyya', and a completion of 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq', and he collected and arranged the fatwas of Siraj al-Din al-Hindi and added to them, finishing in 1138 AH. See: 'Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin' (3: 255), 'Hadiyat al-'Arifin' (2: 318), 'Idah al-Maknun' (2: 202-203). (3) 'Radd al-Muhtar' (1: 48). (4) 'al-Kashf' (2: 1802). (0) He is Muhammad ibn Hamza ibn Muhammad al-Fanari, Shams al-Din. Al-Kafawi said: A great imam, a precise scholar, unique in his time in transmitted sciences and excelling his peers in rational sciences, the sheikh of his age in knowledge and literature. Among his works: 'Fusul al-Bada'i' fi Usul al-Shara'i', 'Sharh Isaghuji', 'Tafsir al-Fatiha', (d. 834 AH). See: 'al-Fawa'id' (pp. 274-276), 'al-Shaqa'iq' (pp. 16-21), and I have devoted a book to him called 'Daw' al-Darari fi Akhbar Shams al-Din al-Fanari'. (6) He is Ahmad ibn Mustafa, famous as Tashkopri Zadeh, Abu al-Khayr 'Isam al-Din. Among his works: 'al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya fi 'Ulama' al-Dawlat al-'Uthmaniyya', 'Miftah al-Sa'ada wa Misbah al-Siyada', and glosses on 'al-Baydawi', (901-968 AH). Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a critical evaluation of various fatwa collections circulating in the Hanafi tradition. The author, likely a later commentator, draws on earlier authorities like al-Birkili and Hajji Khalifa to assess reliability. The text first mentions 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam' by Fakhr al-Din al-Rumi, which al-Birkili counts among weak circulating books. Then 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya' by Fadl Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Ayyub is discussed; al-Birkili explicitly states it is not from the reliable books, and its use is only permissible if it agrees with established principles. The author provides detailed biographical footnotes about al-Haddadi, al-Birkili, and others, showing the chain of authority. On page 57, the text mentions 'Fatawa Ibn Nujaym' and 'Fatawa al-Turi' as reliable sources. Finally, it discusses the famous 'Khulasat al-Kaydani', noting that despite its widespread use, its author is unknown and there are three opinions on its authorship: Shams al-Din al-Fanari, Ibn Kamal Pasha, or another. The passage emphasizes that a mufti must be cautious: popularity does not guarantee reliability; a book must conform to the established Usul (principles) of the school. This reflects the Hanafi concern for scholarly verification and the hierarchy of textual authority.

Key Terms
الفتاوى (al-fatawa): Legal responsa or rulings issued by a mufti, compiled into collections.
المفتي (al-mufti): A qualified jurist who issues legal rulings (fatwas) based on the school's methodology.
الأصول (al-usul): The fundamental principles and established rulings of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is it permissible to act on a fatwa from 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya'?
A) If it is widely circulated among scholars.
B) If it agrees with the established principles (al-usul).
C) If its author is a well-known figure.
D) If it is endorsed by al-Birkili.

Key Takeaway
A fatwa collection's reliability hinges on its author's authority and its conformity to Hanafi usul, not on its fame or frequency of use.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Disputed Authorship of Muqaddimat al-Salah: Principles of Textual Reliability
Critical refinement of authorship dispute and reliability criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four opinions on the authorship of Muqaddimat al-Salah and apply the Hanafi principle that a book's reliability depends on the soundness of its content in addition to the author's standing.

Core Idea
A fiqh text's authority rests on its content's alignment with reliable sources, not merely on the renown of its author.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, the commentator addresses a common challenge for Hanafi students: how to evaluate a short treatise on prayer when its authorship is disputed. He presents four opinions, critiques them, and ultimately defends the treatise based on its widespread acceptance and content, illustrating a key principle in Hanafi textual criticism.

Guided Path
1
List the four opinions
Read the first part of the passage and note each claimed author: (1) Ibn Kamal Pasha, (2) Ibn Hamzah, (3) Lutfallah al-Nasafi, (4) Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi.
2
Critique the fourth opinion
Why is it the weakest? The proposer confused two scholars named al-Nasafi: the author of al-Wafi is Abdullah, not Umar.
3
Analyze the third opinion
Even though it's the most famous, it makes the author unknown (majhul). The text says a majhul author's work is not relied upon unless it agrees with reliable books.
This introduces the principle of content-based reliability.
4
Examine the first two opinions
Both authors are famous (Ibn Kamal Pasha, Ibn Hamzah), but the commentator notes that even a reliable author can produce an unreliable work if it lacks rigor and contains odd issues.
5
Understand the commentator's defense
After studying the treatise, the commentator found it to be reliable and widely commented upon, concluding that its content outweighs concerns about authorship.
This shows the practical application of the principle.
6
Apply the principle
A book's reliability is determined by its content and acceptance by scholars, not solely by the author's fame. An unknown author can produce a reliable work if its content matches authoritative texts.

(٥) أقول : إن جهالة حال المؤلف واقعة في كثير من الكتب كمنية المصلي» للكاشغري وعلى القول الأول والثاني، وإن كان مؤلّفها من المعتبرين، فإنّ ابن كمال باشا وابن حمزة من أجلة عصرهما ، وكَمَلةِ دهرهما كما بسطناه في «الفوائد البهية»(۱) إلا أنّ جمعها بين الرطب واليابس يشهد بعدم اعتبارها ، فكثيراً ما يكون المؤلّف معتبراً في نفسه، ومؤلّفه غير معتبر ؛ لعدم التزامه فيه التنقيد والتنقيح، وجمعه فيه كلّ رطب ويابس من غير تدقيق وتوضيح. والذي ينادي بأعلى النداء على أنها رسالة غير معتبرة، وأن مؤلّفها لا يخلو إما أن يكون ممن لا ممارسة له بالمسائل، ولا علم له بالدلائل، وإما أن يكون لم يلتزم فيها التحقيق والتنقيح ، وإن كان في نفسه من أرباب الترجيح، مطالعة هذه الرسالة من أولها إلى آخرها (٢) ، والاطلاع على مسائلها الشادة، وأحكامها الفاذة، فإنّ فيها مسائل مخالفة (ت ٧٠٥ هـ ) ، ومع ذلك فإنها من الكتب المعتمدة كما نصوا على ذلك ومنهم الإمام اللكنوي فقال في تحفة (الكملة» (ص (٦) : (إنها من الكتب المعتمدة المتداولة، فجهالة مؤلف الكتاب لا تسقط الكتاب إن كانت مسائله معتمدة وإنما معرفة حال المؤلف تزيد من قوة الكتاب ومكانته وهكذا . ينظر : المرقاة شرح مقدمة الصلاة» (ص١٦). (۱) «الفوائد» (ص ٤٢ - ٤٤). (٢) أقول : قد طالعت الرسالة من أولها إلى آخرها وتتبعت مسائلها مسألة مسألة من الكتب المعتبرة، وراجعت بعض شروحها كشرح العلامة عبد الغني النابلسي فوجدتها رسالة بديعة في بابها، لطيفة في منوالها، حري بها أن تشتهر في الخافقين لاشتمالها على دقائق المسائل ، والفروع العديدة في صفحات يسيرة، مما جعل كبار العلماء يتوجهون لشرحها وحل عباراتها كإبراهيم البخاري وطاشكبرى زاده والقهستاني والأقحصاري والسرهندي والقاسمي والسنبهلي والسورتي والأفغاني والخويشكي وغيرهم ممن لا يعدون ولا يحصون. وهذا التلقي والاهتمام من هؤلاء الأئمة الأعلام بها لما وجدوا فيها من الفوائد الجسام التي تتناسب مع المبتدئين من الطلبة فهي صغيرة الحجم كثيرة النفع ، حتي قال إبراهيم البخاري : قد شرحها غير واحد من العلماء، فإنّها مع نهاية صغرها مشتملة على مسائل ضرورية ، يحتاج إليها البرية، مغنية عن مئة مؤلف من المتداولات...» كما في «الكشف»(۲ : ۱۸۰۲). فانتشار هذه الرسالة اللطيفة بين الخافقين وإقبال الطلبة والكملة عليها كان لحسن حالها وبديع نظامها، قال القُهستاني في شرحه عليها: «وقد اشتهرت فيما وراء النهر، اشتهار الشمس في رابعة النهار، وذكر أنه - أي مؤلفها - من مهرة الناظرين عندهم كما في الكشف (۲ : ۱۸۰۲). وأما ما ذكر من جمعها للرطب واليابس، وأن مسائلها غير معتمدة، فإنه محل نظر ؛ فإنني علقت عليها بشرح سميته (المرقاة»، وأمعنت النظر في مسائلها واعتمادها حتى بان لي أن ما خالفت فيه الكتب المعتمدة ينحصر في ذكر مؤلفها لباب من المحرمات وعد تحته بعض المسائل
The commentator Hasan al-Kafi al-Aqhisari, died 1025 AH. Third: It is by al-Fadil Lutfallah al-Nasafi, known as al-Fadil al-Kaidani, mentioned by Shams al-Din al-Quhistani in his commentary, and Ibrahim al-Bukhari in his commentary. And here a fourth opinion mentioned by some contemporaries of Ali al-Qari al-Makki, author of the treatise called 'Tazyin al-‘Ibarah li-Tahsin al-Isharah', and a treatise called 'al-Tadhin li al-Tazyin', that it is by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, Hafiz al-Din ‘Umar, author of 'al-Wafi'. This opinion is the weakest, testifying to the lack of knowledge of its proposer of the conditions of the jurists, for the author of 'al-Wafi' is ‘Abdullah al-Nasafi, author of 'al-Kanz', 'al-Manar', 'al-Madarik', and others, died 701 or 710 AH, and ‘Umar al-Nasafi is someone else, and earlier than him, as he is ‘Umar ibn Muhammad al-Nasafi, nicknamed Mufti al-Thaqalayn, Najm al-Din, author of 'Nazm al-Jami‘ al-Saghir' and 'al-Manzumah fi al-Fiqh', etc., died 537 AH, as we have expanded all that in 'al-Fawa’id al-Bahiyyah fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyyah'. And no one who authored works on the biographies of Hanafis mentioned that 'Muqaddimat al-Salah' is by either of them. As for the three opinions, according to the third one, which is the most famous among the majority, its author is an unknown man, for we have not found in the speech of anyone who authored biographies of Hanafis any news or trace of Lutfallah al-Nasafi. And the unknown person's authorship is not to be relied upon unless it agrees with reliable books. On the first and second opinions, although its author is among the reliable ones — for Ibn Kamal Pasha and Ibn Hamza are among the greats of their era and the perfect of their time, as we expanded in 'al-Fawa’id al-Bahiyyah' — yet its compilation of dry and wet testifies to its unreliability. For often the author is reliable in himself, but his work is unreliable due to his lack of commitment to criticism and refinement, and his compilation of every dry and wet without precision and clarification. And that which calls out loudly that this treatise is unreliable, and that its author is either someone with no practice in issues and no knowledge of proofs, or someone who did not commit to verification and refinement even if he himself was among the people of tarjih, is reading this treatise from beginning to end and examining its odd issues and unique rulings, for it contains issues contradicting (the reliable books). Yet despite that, it is among the relied upon books as they have stated, including Imam al-Laknawi who said in Tuhfat al-Kumlah (p.6): 'It is among the relied upon and circulated books. Ignorance of the author does not nullify the book if its issues are reliable. Rather, knowledge of the author's status increases the book's strength and standing, and so on.' See: al-Marqat Sharh Muqaddimat al-Salah (p.16). I have read the treatise from beginning to end and traced its issues one by one from the reliable books, and reviewed some of its commentaries such as the commentary of ‘Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, and found it to be a unique treatise in its topic, elegant in its style, worthy of becoming famous in the East and West for containing subtle issues and numerous branches in few pages, which made senior scholars turn to comment on it and explain its expressions, such as Ibrahim al-Bukhari, Tashkopruzadeh, al-Quhistani, al-Aqhisari, al-Sirhindi, al-Qasimi, al-Sanbuhli, al-Surti, al-Afghani, al-Khuwaishki, and others too numerous to count. This reception and interest from these eminent imams in it was because they found in it great benefits suitable for beginners among students, so it is small in size but great in benefit. Even Ibrahim al-Bukhari said: 'More than one scholar has commented on it, for despite its extreme smallness, it contains necessary issues that the creation needs, making it sufficient instead of a hundred commonly circulated works...' as in al-Kashf (2:1802). The spread of this elegant treatise between East and West and the acceptance of students and the perfect towards it was due to its good condition and beautiful organization. Al-Quhistani said in his commentary on it: 'It has become famous beyond the river, like the sun at midday,' and he mentioned that its author was among the skilled researchers in their view, as in al-Kashf (2:1802). As for the mention of its compilation of dry and wet and that its issues are unreliable, that is subject to consideration; for I have attached a commentary to it called 'al-Marqat', and have pondered deeply over its issues and reliability until it became clear to me that its disagreement with reliable books is limited to the author's mention of a chapter on prohibited things and listing under it some issues.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiyah) from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāyah, a super-commentary on Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah. The author discusses the disputed authorship of a famous treatise on prayer (Muqaddimat al-Ṣalāh) and its reliability. Four opinions are mentioned: (1) it is by Ibn Kamāl Pāshā, (2) by Ibn Ḥamzah, (3) by al-Fāḍil Luṭfallāh al-Nasafī (al-Kaydānī), and (4) by Abū al-Barakāt al-Nasafī. The fourth is dismissed as the weakest due to confusion between two scholars named al-Nasafī. The third opinion, though famous, makes the author unknown. The first two opinions name reliable authors, but the work itself is criticized for lacking rigor. However, the commentator then defends the treatise after studying it, noting its widespread acceptance and many commentaries, arguing that its issues are mostly reliable and that the criticism is limited to minor points. He emphasizes that a book's reliability depends on its content, not solely on the author's fame — a principle supported by Imam al-Laknawī.

Key Terms
مقدمة الصلاة (Muqaddimat al-Ṣalāh): A short treatise on the rulings of prayer, whose authorship is disputed in this passage.
الفوائد البهية في تراجم الحنفية (al-Fawā’id al-Bahiyyah fī Tarājim al-Ḥanafiyyah): A biographical work by the commentator himself, referenced for details on Hanafi scholars.
المجهول (al-majhūl): An unknown person; a book by an unknown author is not relied upon unless its content matches authoritative works.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which opinion on the authorship of Muqaddimat al-Salah is considered the weakest?
A) That it is by Ibn Kamal Pasha
B) That it is by Ibn Hamzah
C) That it is by Lutfallah al-Nasafi
D) That it is by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi

Key Takeaway
The authority of a fiqh treatise is determined by its content and scholarly acceptance, not merely by the fame of its author.
