Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Author's Methodological Note on Biographical Entries
Concluding remarks on biographical studies and author's methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's rationale for omitting detailed biographical entries and identify the primary sources where such information can be found.

Core Idea
Biographical detail is omitted for brevity; the scholar's method prioritises concise, need-based learning.

This passage from 'Umadat al-Ri'ayah marks a transition from the ninth study on biographical entries to the main commentary. The author explains his decision to omit extensive biographical details from this work, directing readers to his other writings for completeness. This reveals a key pedagogical principle in classical Hanafi scholarship: tailoring content to the immediate needs of the reader while preserving depth in auxiliary works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
Read the passage and determine why the author chose to omit biographical entries. Look for key phrases like 'I saw that deleting them here is more appropriate' and 'seeking brevity'.
The author is not discarding information but redirecting it.
2
Recognize the cross-referencing strategy
Note how the author mentions his earlier work 'Muqaddimah al-Sa'ayah' and his 'Hashiyah' as the proper places for detailed biographical and contextual information.
This shows the intertextual nature of classical Hanafi scholarship.
3
Analyze the pedagogical rationale
Consider why a commentator would choose brevity. The phrase 'to the extent of need' suggests a focus on essential knowledge, avoiding digression that might distract from the main subject.
This reflects the principle of 'al-iqtisar 'ala qadr al-hajah' (limiting to the extent of need).
4
Apply the method to other texts
When studying a Hanafi commentary, consider how the author balances comprehensiveness with brevity. Ask: what is assumed to be known? Where can I find more details?
This skill is crucial for independent study of classical texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة التاسعة تراجم الأعيان في الشرح
ثم أجاب عن إيرادات صدر الشريعة، ونصر جده، وحقق أقواله المنيفة، وستقف عليه في موضعه إن شاء الله تعالى هذا آخر الكلام في هذا المقام. وقد ذكرت في «مقدمة السعاية» أحوال الكتب التي نقل عنها صدر الشريعة المسائل وغيرها، وأحوال النسب والقبائل والأمكنة المذكورة في «شرح الوقاية»، وتراجم شراح «مختصر الوقاية». ورأيت حذفها هاهنا أجدر طلباً للاقتصار على قدر الحاجة، وترك ما عنه غنية، وستطلعُ في «الحاشية» في كل موضع على ما يناسبها على وجه يفيد الطالب بصيرة ويغنه، وهذا أوانُ الشروع في المقصود ، متوكلاً على فائض الخير والجود.
The ninth study: biographical entries of notable figures in the commentary. Then he answered the objections of Sadr al-Shari'ah, and supported his grandfather, and verified his lofty statements. And you will find it in its place, if Allah wills. This is the end of speech in this regard. And I have mentioned in 'Muqaddimah al-Sa'ayah' the conditions of the books from which Sadr al-Shari'ah transmitted the issues and others, and the conditions of lineages, tribes, and places mentioned in 'Sharh al-Wiqayah', and the biographies of the commentators of 'Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah'. And I saw that deleting them here is more appropriate, seeking brevity to the extent of need, and leaving what is unnecessary. And you will look into the 'Hashiyah' in every place for what is appropriate in a way that benefits the student with insight and enriches him. And this is the time to begin the intended subject, relying on the overflowing of goodness and generosity.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a transitional section from the author of 'Umadat al-Ri'ayah, a super-commentary (hāshiyah) on 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'. It concludes the ninth study, which dealt with biographical entries (tarājim al-a'yān) of scholars mentioned in the commentary. The author states that the commentator (probably the grandfather, referring to the author of 'Sharh al-Wiqayah') has responded to objections raised by Sadr al-Shari'ah, supported his grandfather's views, and verified his statements. The author then explains his own methodology: he had previously compiled detailed information about the sources used by Sadr al-Shari'ah and biographies of commentators in his work 'Muqaddimah al-Sa'ayah'. However, he chooses to omit those details here for the sake of brevity, directing the reader to his 'Hashiyah' for relevant insights. This reflects the author's pedagogical approach: providing concise yet comprehensive coverage while ensuring that students have access to deeper material elsewhere. He now announces his readiness to begin the main subject of the book, relying on divine grace.

Key Terms
تراجم الأعيان (tarājim al-a'yān): Biographical entries of notable figures (scholars) discussed in the commentary.
صدر الشريعة (Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah): A reference to a prominent Hanafi scholar, likely Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Thānī (ʻUbayd Allāh ibn Masʻūd al-Maḥbūbī), author of 'Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah' or 'al-Wiqāyah'.
مقدمة السعاية (Muqaddimah al-Sa'āyah): A separate work by the author of 'Umadat al-Ri'āyah, serving as an introduction containing detailed accounts of books, lineages, and biographies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author of 'Umadat al-Ri'ayah omit detailed biographical entries in this work?
A) He considers them unimportant.
B) For brevity, referring readers to his other works.
C) He lost the original manuscripts.
D) The publisher refused to include them.

Key Takeaway
The author's methodological choice to omit biographical details reflects a pedagogical principle of conciseness, directing serious students to dedicated works for deeper context.
